The methods used by the Stalinists against the Opposition became more and more extreme. At the XV Party Conference in October 1926, Trotsky could barely speak because of interruptions and catcalls, and at the end of the Conference he lost his Politburo seat. In 1927, Stalin started using the [GPU](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gosudarstvennoye_Politicheskoye_Upravlenie "Gosudarstvennoye Politicheskoye Upravlenie") (Soviet secret police) to infiltrate and discredit the opposition. Rank-and-file oppositionists were increasingly harassed, sometimes expelled from the Party and even arrested.

Soviet policy toward the Chinese Revolution became the ideological line of demarcation between Stalin and the United Opposition. The Chinese Revolution began on 10 October 1911,<sup id="cite_ref-184"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-184">[174]</a></sup> resulting in the abdication of the Chinese Emperor, [Puyi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Puyi "Puyi"), on 12 February 1912.<sup id="cite_ref-185"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-185">[175]</a></sup> [Sun Yat-sen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sun_Yat-sen "Sun Yat-sen") established the [Republic of China](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Republic_of_China_(1912%E2%80%9349) "Republic of China (1912–49)"). In reality, however, the Republic controlled very little of the country. Much of China was divided between various regional warlords. The Republican government established a new "nationalist people's army and a national people's party"—the [Kuomintang](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuomintang "Kuomintang"). In 1920, the Kuomintang opened relations with Soviet Russia. With Soviet help, the Republic of China built up the nationalist people's army. With the development of the nationalist army, a [Northern Expedition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northern_Expedition "Northern Expedition") was planned to smash the power of the warlords of the northern part of the country. This Northern Expedition became a point of contention over foreign policy by Stalin and Trotsky. Stalin tried to persuade the small Chinese [Communist Party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communist_Party_of_China "Communist Party of China") to merge with the Kuomintang (KMT) Nationalists to bring about a bourgeois revolution before attempting to bring about a Soviet-style working class revolution.<sup id="cite_ref-186"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-186">[176]</a></sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Joseph_Stalin_and_Leon_Trotsky_at_Felix_Dzerzhinsky_funeral.jpg/220px-Joseph_Stalin_and_Leon_Trotsky_at_Felix_Dzerzhinsky_funeral.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Joseph_Stalin_and_Leon_Trotsky_at_Felix_Dzerzhinsky_funeral.jpg)

[Kalinin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mikhail_Kalinin "Mikhail Kalinin") and [Stalin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stalin "Stalin") bearing the coffin of [Felix Dzerzhinsky](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Felix_Dzerzhinsky "Felix Dzerzhinsky") on 22 July 1926. Trotsky can be seen over Kalinin's left shoulder.

Trotsky wanted the Communist Party to complete an orthodox proletarian revolution and have clear class independence from the KMT. Stalin funded the KMT during the expedition.<sup id="cite_ref-187"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-187">[177]</a></sup> Stalin countered Trotskyist criticism by making a secret speech in which he said that [Chiang Kai-shek](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chiang_Kai-shek "Chiang Kai-shek")'s right-wing Kuomintang were the only ones capable of defeating the imperialists, that Chiang had funding from the rich merchants, and that his forces were to be utilized until squeezed for all usefulness like a lemon before being discarded. However, Chiang quickly reversed the tables in the [Shanghai massacre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shanghai_massacre "Shanghai massacre") of 12 April 1927 by massacring the Communist Party in Shanghai midway through the Northern Expedition.<sup id="cite_ref-188"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-188">[178]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-189"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-189">[179]</a></sup>

### Defeat and exile (1927–1928)\[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Leon_Trotsky&action=edit&section=27 "Edit section: Defeat and exile (1927–1928)")\]

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Leon_Trotsky_1928.jpg/220px-Leon_Trotsky_1928.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Leon_Trotsky_1928.jpg)

Trotsky with his wife Natalia and son Lev in Alma Ata, 1928

On the tenth anniversary of the October Revolution, the Opposition held a street demonstration, and Trotsky was expelled from the Communist Party shortly after.<sup id="cite_ref-190"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-190">[180]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-191"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-191">[181]</a></sup> Trotsky gave the eulogy at the funeral of his friend, the Soviet diplomat [Adolph Joffe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adolph_Joffe "Adolph Joffe"), in November 1927. It would be the last speech that Trotsky would give in the Soviet Union. When the XV Party Congress made United Opposition views incompatible with membership in the Communist Party, Zinoviev, Kamenev, and their supporters capitulated and renounced their alliance with the Left Opposition. Trotsky and most of his followers, on the other hand, refused to surrender and stayed the course. Trotsky was exiled to [Alma Ata, Kazakhstan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Almaty "Almaty") on 31 January 1928. He was expelled from the Soviet Union to Turkey in February 1929, accompanied by his wife Natalia Sedova and their eldest son, Lev.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERubenstein2013155,_202_192-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTERubenstein2013155,_202-192">[182]</a></sup>

### Fate of Left Oppositionists after Trotsky's exile (1929–1941)\[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Leon_Trotsky&action=edit&section=28 "Edit section: Fate of Left Oppositionists after Trotsky's exile (1929–1941)")\]

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Soviet_reaction_to_Leon_Trotsky_publication.jpg/220px-Soviet_reaction_to_Leon_Trotsky_publication.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Soviet_reaction_to_Leon_Trotsky_publication.jpg)

The publication of Trotsky's autobiography _[My Life](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/My_Life_(Leon_Trotsky_autobiography) "My Life (Leon Trotsky autobiography)")_ as reported in the Soviet Union in August 1929, with the editors of _Projector_ titled the publication: "On the service of bourgeoisie"

After Trotsky's expulsion from the Soviet Union, Trotskyists within the Soviet Union began to waver. Between 1929 and 1932, most leading members of the Left Opposition surrendered to Stalin, "admitted their mistakes" and were reinstated in the Communist Party. One initial exception to this was [Christian Rakovsky](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christian_Rakovsky "Christian Rakovsky"), who inspired Trotsky between 1929 and 1934 with his refusal to capitulate as state suppression of any remaining opposition to Stalin increased by the year. In late 1932, Rakovsky had failed with an attempt to flee the Soviet Union and was exiled to [Yakutia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yakutia "Yakutia") in March 1933. Answering Trotsky's request, the French mathematician and Trotskyist [Jean Van Heijenoort](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jean_Van_Heijenoort "Jean Van Heijenoort"), together with his fellow activist [Pierre Frank](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pierre_Frank "Pierre Frank"), unsuccessfully called on the influential Soviet author [Maxim Gorky](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maxim_Gorky "Maxim Gorky") to intervene in favor of Christian Rakovsky, and boarded the ship he was traveling on near Constantinople.<sup id="cite_ref-yedlin_193-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-yedlin-193">[183]</a></sup> According to Heijenoort, they only managed to meet Gorky's son, Maxim Peshkov, who reportedly told them that his father was indisposed, but promised to pass on their request.<sup id="cite_ref-yedlin_193-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-yedlin-193">[183]</a></sup> Rakovsky was the last prominent Trotskyist to capitulate to Stalin in April 1934, when Rakovsky formally "admitted his mistakes" (his letter to _Pravda_, titled _There Should Be No Mercy_, depicted Trotsky and his supporters as "agents of the German [Gestapo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gestapo "Gestapo")").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMedvedev1976169_194-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMedvedev1976169-194">[184]</a></sup> Rakovsky was appointed to high office in the Commissariat for Health and allowed to return to Moscow, also serving as Soviet ambassador to Japan in 1935.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFeofanovBarry199522_195-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFeofanovBarry199522-195">[185]</a></sup> However, Rakovsky was cited in allegations involving the killing of [Sergey Kirov](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sergey_Kirov "Sergey Kirov"), and was arrested and imprisoned in late 1937, during the Great Purge.<sup id="cite_ref-faganoppexile_196-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-faganoppexile-196">[186]</a></sup>

Almost all Trotskyists who were still within the Soviet Union's borders were executed in the Great Purges of 1936–1938, although Rakovsky survived until the [Medvedev Forest massacre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Medvedev_Forest_massacre "Medvedev Forest massacre") of September 1941, where he was shot dead along with 156 other prisoners on Stalin's orders, less than three months into the [Axis invasion of the Soviet Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Axis_invasion_of_the_Soviet_Union "Axis invasion of the Soviet Union"). Also among the Medvedev Forest victims was Trotsky's sister/Kamenev's first wife, [Olga Kameneva](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Olga_Kameneva "Olga Kameneva").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEParrish199669_16-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTEParrish199669-16">[13]</a></sup>

## Exile (1929–1940)\[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Leon_Trotsky&action=edit&section=29 "Edit section: Exile (1929–1940)")\]

### Turkey\[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Leon_Trotsky&action=edit&section=30 "Edit section: Turkey")\]

After being deported from the Soviet Union, in February 1929, Trotsky arrived in Turkey. During his first two months in Turkey, Trotsky lived with his wife and eldest son at the [Soviet Union Consulate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_diplomatic_missions_of_Russia "List of diplomatic missions of Russia") in [Istanbul](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Istanbul "Istanbul") and then at a nearby hotel in the city. In April 1929, Trotsky, his wife and son were moved to the island of [Büyükada](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/B%C3%BCy%C3%BCkada "Büyükada") by the Turkish authorities. On Büyükada, they were moved into a house called the Yanaros mansion.<sup id="cite_ref-197"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-197">[187]</a></sup> During his exile in Turkey, Trotsky was under the surveillance of the Turkish police forces of [Mustafa Kemal Pasha](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mustafa_Kemal_Pasha "Mustafa Kemal Pasha"). Trotsky was also at risk from the many former White Army officers who lived on Prinkipo, officers who had opposed the [October Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/October_Revolution "October Revolution") and who had been defeated by Trotsky and the Red Army in the Russian Civil War. However, Trotsky's European supporters volunteered to serve as bodyguards and assured his safety.<sup id="cite_ref-marxists.org_198-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-marxists.org-198">[188]</a></sup> At this time, he made requests to enter Belgium, France, Norway, Germany, and the United Kingdom,<sup id="cite_ref-199"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-199">[189]</a></sup> but all refused access.

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Trotsky_House_Istanbul.jpg/220px-Trotsky_House_Istanbul.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Trotsky_House_Istanbul.jpg)

Trotsky's house, the Yanaros mansion on the island of [Büyükada](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/B%C3%BCy%C3%BCkada "Büyükada") in Turkey, as it appears today. Trotsky lived at the house from April 1929 until July 1933.

In 1931, Trotsky wrote a letter to a friend entitled "What is Fascism" in which he attempted to [define fascism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Definitions_of_fascism#Leon_Trotsky "Definitions of fascism") and asserted that the [Communist International](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communist_International "Communist International") was wrong to describe the [dictatorship of Primo de Rivera](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dictatorship_of_Primo_de_Rivera "Dictatorship of Primo de Rivera") as "[fascist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fascist "Fascist")" because it was not a mass movement arising from a base in the lower classes.<sup id="cite_ref-200"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-200">[190]</a></sup>

On 20 February 1932, Trotsky and all of his family lost their Soviet citizenship and were forbidden to enter the Soviet Union.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESwain2006191_201-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTESwain2006191-201">[191]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-202"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-202">[192]</a></sup> In 1932, Trotsky entered via a port into the fascist [Kingdom of Italy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy "Kingdom of Italy")<sup id="cite_ref-203"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-203">[193]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-204"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-204">[194]</a></sup> on his way to a socialist conference in Denmark.<sup id="cite_ref-205"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-205">[195]</a></sup> By the end of 1932, Trotsky had made contact with the anti-Stalin opposition inside the USSR and discussed the possibility of forming a bloc.<sup id="cite_ref-206"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-206">[196]</a></sup> There was no evidence of any alliance with [Nazi Germany](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazi_Germany "Nazi Germany") or [Japan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Empire_of_Japan "Empire of Japan"), as the Soviet Union government claimed. The alleged members of the anti-Stalin bloc were Zinovievites, [rightists](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Right_Opposition "Right Opposition") and Trotskyists who "capitulated" to Stalin. Kamenev and Zinoviev were also alleged members of the bloc. Trotsky wanted by no means that the alliance became a fusion, and he was afraid of the right gaining much power inside the bloc. Historian [Pierre Broué](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pierre_Brou%C3%A9 "Pierre Broué") concluded that the bloc dissolved in early 1933, since some of its members like Zinoviev and Kamenev joined Stalin again, and because there were no letters in the Trotsky Harvard archive mentioning the bloc after 1932.<sup id="cite_ref-207"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-207">[197]</a></sup>

### France\[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Leon_Trotsky&action=edit&section=31 "Edit section: France")\]

In July 1933, Trotsky was offered asylum in France by Prime Minister [Édouard Daladier](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C3%89douard_Daladier "Édouard Daladier"). Trotsky accepted the offer, but he was forbidden to live in [Paris](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paris "Paris") and soon found himself under the surveillance of the French police. From July 1933 to February 1934, Trotsky and his wife lived in [Royan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Royan "Royan"). The philosopher and activist [Simone Weil](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Simone_Weil "Simone Weil") also arranged for Trotsky and his bodyguards to stay for a few days at her parents' house.<sup id="cite_ref-marxists.org_198-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-marxists.org-198">[188]</a></sup> Following the [6 February 1934 crisis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/6_February_1934_crisis "6 February 1934 crisis") in France, the French minister of internal affairs, [Albert Sarraut](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Sarraut "Albert Sarraut"), signed a decree to deport Trotsky from France.<sup id="cite_ref-marxists.org_198-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-marxists.org-198">[188]</a></sup> However, no foreign government was found willing to accept Trotsky within its borders. Accordingly, the French authorities instructed Trotsky to move to a residence in the tiny village of [Barbizon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barbizon "Barbizon") under the strict surveillance of the French police, where Trotsky found his contact with the outside world to be even worse than during his exile in Turkey.<sup id="cite_ref-marxists.org_198-3"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-marxists.org-198">[188]</a></sup>

In May 1935, soon after the French government had agreed to the [Franco-Soviet Treaty of Mutual Assistance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franco-Soviet_Treaty_of_Mutual_Assistance "Franco-Soviet Treaty of Mutual Assistance") with the Soviet Union government, Trotsky was officially told that he was no longer welcome in France. After weighing his options, Trotsky applied to move to Norway.

### Norway\[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Leon_Trotsky&action=edit&section=32 "Edit section: Norway")\]

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Heradsbygdveien_26%2C_H%C3%B8nefoss.jpg/220px-Heradsbygdveien_26%2C_H%C3%B8nefoss.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Heradsbygdveien_26,_H%C3%B8nefoss.jpg)

Konrad Knudsen's House in Veksal, Norderhov, Norway, where Trotsky lived from June 1935 to September 1936

After obtaining permission from Justice Minister [Trygve Lie](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trygve_Lie "Trygve Lie") to enter the country, Trotsky and his wife became a guest of [Konrad Knudsen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Konrad_Knudsen "Konrad Knudsen") at [Norderhov](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Norderhov "Norderhov"), near [Hønefoss](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/H%C3%B8nefoss "Hønefoss"), and spent over a year living at Knudsen's house, from 18 June 1935 to 2 September 1936. Trotsky was hospitalized for a few weeks at the nearby [Oslo Community Hospital](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oslo_University_Hospital,_Ullev%C3%A5l "Oslo University Hospital, Ullevål"), from 19 September 1935.<sup id="cite_ref-Swain_208-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-Swain-208">[198]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-209"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-209">[199]</a></sup>

Following French media complaints about Trotsky's role in encouraging the [mass strikes in France in May and June 1936](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Matignon_Agreements_(1936) "Matignon Agreements (1936)") with his articles, the [Johan Nygaardsvold](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johan_Nygaardsvold "Johan Nygaardsvold")\-led Norwegian government began to exhibit disquiet about Trotsky's actions. In the summer of 1936, Trotsky's asylum was increasingly made a political issue by the fascist [Nasjonal Samling](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nasjonal_Samling "Nasjonal Samling"), led by [Vidkun Quisling](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vidkun_Quisling "Vidkun Quisling"), along with an increase in pressure from the Soviet government on the Norwegian authorities. On 5 August 1936, Knudsen's house was burgled by fascists from the Nasjonal Samling while Trotsky and his wife were out on a seashore trip with Knudsen and his wife. The burglars targeted Trotsky's works and archives for vandalism. The raid was largely thwarted by Knudsen's daughter, Hjørdis, although the burglars did take a few papers from the nearest table as they left.<sup id="cite_ref-auto1_211-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-auto1-211">[201]</a></sup> Although the perpetrators were caught and put on trial, the "evidence" obtained in the burglary was used by the government to make claims against Trotsky.<sup id="cite_ref-author_210-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-author-210">[200]</a></sup> 

On 14 August 1936, the Soviet Press Agency [TASS](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Telegraph_Agency_of_the_Soviet_Union "Telegraph Agency of the Soviet Union") announced the discovery of a "Trotskyist–Zinovievist" plot and the imminent start of the [Moscow trials](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moscow_trials "Moscow trials") of the accused. Trotsky demanded a complete and open enquiry into Moscow's accusations. The accused were sentenced to death, including Grigory Zinoviev and Lev Kamenev, and executed on 25 August 1936. On 26 August 1936, eight policemen arrived at Knudsen's house demanding that Trotsky sign new conditions for residing in Norway. These conditions included agreeing to write no more about current political matters, to give no interviews, and to have all his correspondence (incoming and outgoing) inspected by the police. Trotsky categorically refused the conditions, and Trotsky was then told that he and his wife would soon be moved to another residence.<sup id="cite_ref-auto1_211-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-auto1-211">[201]</a></sup> The following day Trotsky was interrogated by the police about his political activities, with the police officially citing Trotsky as a "witness" to the fascist raid of 5 August 1936.<sup id="cite_ref-212"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-212">[202]</a></sup>

On 2 September 1936, four weeks after the break-in at Knudsen's house, Trygve Lie ordered that Trotsky and his wife be transferred to a farm in [Hurum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hurum "Hurum"),<sup id="cite_ref-Hurum_213-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-Hurum-213">[203]</a></sup> where they were under house arrest.<sup id="cite_ref-author_210-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-author-210">[200]</a></sup> The treatment of Trotsky and his wife at Hurum was harsh, as they were forced to stay indoors for 22 hours per day under the constant guard of thirteen policemen, with only one hour permitted twice a day for a walk on the farm.<sup id="cite_ref-author_210-3"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-author-210">[200]</a></sup> Trotsky was prevented from posting any letters and prevented from arguing back against his critics in Norway and beyond. Only Trotsky's lawyers and the [Norwegian Labour Party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Norwegian_Labour_Party "Norwegian Labour Party") Parliamentary leader, [Olav Scheflo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Olav_Scheflo "Olav Scheflo"), were permitted to visit.<sup id="cite_ref-author_210-4"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-author-210">[200]</a></sup> From October 1936, even the outdoor walks were prohibited for Trotsky and his wife.<sup id="cite_ref-author_210-5"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-author-210">[200]</a></sup> Trotsky did eventually manage to smuggle out one letter on 18 December 1936, titled _The Moscow "Confessions"_.<sup id="cite_ref-214"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-214">[204]</a></sup> On 19 December 1936, Trotsky and his wife were deported from Norway after being put on the Norwegian oil tanker _Ruth_, under guard by [Jonas Lie](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jonas_Lie_(government_minister) "Jonas Lie (government minister)"). When later living in Mexico, Trotsky was utterly scathing about the treatment he received during his 108 days at [Hurum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hurum "Hurum"), and accused the Norwegian government of trying to prevent him from publicly voicing his strong opposition to the Moscow Trials and other show trials, saying:

> When I look back today on this period of internment, I must say that never, anywhere, in the course of my entire life—and I have lived through many things—was I persecuted with as much miserable cynicism as I was by the Norwegian "Socialist" government. For four months, these ministers, dripping with democratic hypocrisy, gripped me in a stranglehold to prevent me from protesting the greatest crime history may ever know.<sup id="cite_ref-author_210-6"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-author-210">[200]</a></sup> 

### Mexico\[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Leon_Trotsky&action=edit&section=33 "Edit section: Mexico")\]

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Leon_Trotsky_House%2C_Mexico_City_%287144251529%29.jpg/220px-Leon_Trotsky_House%2C_Mexico_City_%287144251529%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Leon_Trotsky_House,_Mexico_City_(7144251529).jpg)

Trotsky's house in [Mexico City](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mexico_City "Mexico City") from April 1939 until his assassination in August 1940

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Trotsky_%26_Khalo.jpg/220px-Trotsky_%26_Khalo.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Trotsky_%26_Khalo.jpg)

Trotsky arrives in Mexico, January 1937 with his wife. Artist [Frida Kahlo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frida_Kahlo "Frida Kahlo") behind them.

[](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Trotsky_Speech_In_Mexico_(1930-1939).webm "Play video")Duration: 3 minutes and 35 seconds.[](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Trotsky_Speech_In_Mexico_(1930-1939).webm)

A speech of Trotsky in Mexico, where he thanks Mexico and President Lázaro Cárdenas for receiving him, and says that Stalin's trial against him is based on false evidence

The _Ruth_ arrived in Mexico on 9 January 1937.<sup id="cite_ref-author_210-7"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-author-210">[200]</a></sup> On Trotsky's arrival, the Mexican president, [Lázaro Cárdenas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/L%C3%A1zaro_C%C3%A1rdenas "Lázaro Cárdenas"), welcomed Trotsky to Mexico and arranged for his special train _The Hidalgo_ to bring Trotsky to Mexico City from the port of [Tampico](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tampico "Tampico").<sup id="cite_ref-215"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-215">[205]</a></sup>

From January 1937 to April 1939, Trotsky and his wife lived in the [Coyoacán](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coyoac%C3%A1n "Coyoacán") area of Mexico City at [La Casa Azul (The Blue House)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/La_Casa_Azul_(The_Blue_House) "La Casa Azul (The Blue House)"), the home of the painter [Diego Rivera](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diego_Rivera "Diego Rivera") and Rivera's wife and fellow painter, [Frida Kahlo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frida_Kahlo "Frida Kahlo"), with whom Trotsky had an affair.<sup id="cite_ref-216"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-216">[206]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Patenaude,_Bertrand_217-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-Patenaude,_Bertrand-217">[207]</a></sup> She later presented him with _[Self-Portrait Dedicated to Leon Trotsky](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Self-Portrait_Dedicated_to_Leon_Trotsky "Self-Portrait Dedicated to Leon Trotsky")_ on his birthday, the 20th anniversary of the October Revolution.<sup id="cite_ref-kettenmann_218-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-kettenmann-218">[208]</a></sup> His final move was a few blocks away to a residence on Avenida Viena in April 1939, following a break with Rivera.<sup id="cite_ref-Patenaude,_Bertrand_217-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-Patenaude,_Bertrand-217">[207]</a></sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/17/Trotskycannon.felixmorrow.jpg/170px-Trotskycannon.felixmorrow.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Trotskycannon.felixmorrow.jpg)

[James Cannon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/James_P._Cannon "James P. Cannon") and [Felix Morrow](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Felix_Morrow "Felix Morrow") with a bust of Trotsky

Trotsky wrote prolifically while in exile, penning several key works, including his _[History of the Russian Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_Russian_Revolution "History of the Russian Revolution")_ (1930) and _[The Revolution Betrayed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Revolution_Betrayed "The Revolution Betrayed")_ (1936), a critique of the Soviet Union under [Stalinism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stalinism "Stalinism"). He argued that the Soviet state had become a "[degenerated workers' state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Degenerated_workers%27_state "Degenerated workers' state")" controlled by an undemocratic bureaucracy, which would eventually either be overthrown via a [political revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Political_revolution_(Trotskyism) "Political revolution (Trotskyism)") establishing a workers' democracy, or degenerate into a capitalist class.<sup id="cite_ref-219"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-219">[209]</a></sup>

While in Mexico, Trotsky also worked closely with [James Cannon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/James_P._Cannon "James P. Cannon"), [Joseph Hansen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_Hansen_(socialist) "Joseph Hansen (socialist)"), and [Farrell Dobbs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Farrell_Dobbs "Farrell Dobbs") of the [Socialist Workers Party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Socialist_Workers_Party_(United_States) "Socialist Workers Party (United States)") of the United States, and other supporters.<sup id="cite_ref-220"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-220">[210]</a></sup> Cannon, a long-time leading member of the American communist movement, had supported Trotsky in the struggle against Stalinism since he had first read Trotsky's criticisms of the Soviet Union in 1928. Trotsky's critique of the Stalinist regime, though banned, was distributed to leaders of the Comintern. Among his other supporters was [Chen Duxiu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chen_Duxiu "Chen Duxiu"), founder of the [Chinese Communist Party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chinese_Communist_Party "Chinese Communist Party").<sup id="cite_ref-221"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-221">[211]</a></sup>

While in Mexico, Trotsky worked with [André Breton](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Andr%C3%A9_Breton "André Breton") and Diego Rivera to write the [Manifesto for an Independent Revolutionary Art](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manifesto_for_an_Independent_Revolutionary_Art "Manifesto for an Independent Revolutionary Art"), which inspired the creation of the organization, the International Federation of Independent Revolutionary Art (FIARI) in 1938. This organization was short-lived and ended before 1940.

### Moscow show trials\[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Leon_Trotsky&action=edit&section=34 "Edit section: Moscow show trials")\]

In August 1936, the first Moscow show trial of the so-called "Trotskyite–Zinovievite Terrorist Center" was staged in front of an international audience. During the trial, Zinoviev, Kamenev and 14 other accused, most of them prominent Old Bolsheviks, confessed to having plotted with Trotsky to kill Stalin and other members of the Soviet leadership. The court found every defendant guilty, [in absentia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trial_in_absentia "Trial in absentia"), including Trotsky, sentencing them to death. The second show trial of Karl Radek, [Grigori Sokolnikov](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grigori_Sokolnikov "Grigori Sokolnikov"), [Yuri Pyatakov](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yuri_Pyatakov "Yuri Pyatakov"), and 14 others, took place in January 1937, during which more alleged conspiracies and crimes were linked to Trotsky. The findings were published in the book "Not Guilty".<sup id="cite_ref-222"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-222">[212]</a></sup>

> The Moscow trials are perpetuated under the banner of socialism. We will not concede this banner to the masters of falsehood! If our generation happens to be too weak to establish Socialism over the earth, we will hand the spotless banner down to our children. The struggle which is in the offing transcends by far the importance of individuals, factions and parties. It is the struggle for the future of all mankind. It will be severe, it will be lengthy. Whoever seeks physical comfort and spiritual calm let him step aside. In time of reaction it is more convenient to lean on the bureaucracy than on the truth. But all those for whom the word 'Socialism' is not a hollow sound but the content of their moral life—forward! Neither threats nor persecutions nor violations can stop us! Be it even over our bleaching bones the future will triumph! We will blaze the trail for it. It will conquer! Under all the severe blows of fate, I shall be happy as in the best days of my youth; because, my friends, the highest human happiness is not the exploitation of the present but the preparation of the future."
> 
> — Leon Trotsky, 'I Stake My Life', opening address to the [Dewey Commission](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dewey_Commission "Dewey Commission"), 9 February 1937<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENorth2010viii_223-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTENorth2010viii-223">[213]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-224"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-224">[214]</a></sup>

### Fourth International\[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Leon_Trotsky&action=edit&section=35 "Edit section: Fourth International")\]

For fear of splitting the communist movement, Trotsky initially opposed the idea of establishing parallel communist parties or a parallel international communist organization that would compete with the Third International. In mid-1933, after the [Nazi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazi "Nazi") takeover in Germany and the Comintern's response to it, he changed his mind. He said:<sup id="cite_ref-225"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-225">[215]</a></sup>

> An organization which was not roused by the thunder of fascism and which submits docilely to such outrageous acts of the bureaucracy demonstrates thereby that it is dead and that nothing can ever revive it... In all our subsequent work it is necessary to take as our point of departure the historical collapse of the official Communist International.<sup id="cite_ref-226"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-226">[216]</a></sup>

In 1938, Trotsky and his supporters founded the [Fourth International](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fourth_International "Fourth International"), which was intended to be a revolutionary and internationalist alternative to the Stalinist Comintern.

### The Dies Committee\[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Leon_Trotsky&action=edit&section=36 "Edit section: The Dies Committee")\]

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Leon_Trotsky_and_American_admirers._Mexico_-_NARA_-_283642.jpg/220px-Leon_Trotsky_and_American_admirers._Mexico_-_NARA_-_283642.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Leon_Trotsky_and_American_admirers._Mexico_-_NARA_-_283642.jpg)

Trotsky with American comrades, including [Harry DeBoer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_DeBoer "Harry DeBoer") (left) in Mexico, shortly before his assassination, 1940

Towards the end of 1939, Trotsky agreed to go to the United States to appear as a witness before the Dies Committee of the House of Representatives, a forerunner of the [House Committee on Un-American Activities](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/House_Committee_on_Un-American_Activities "House Committee on Un-American Activities"). Representative [Martin Dies Jr.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Martin_Dies_Jr. "Martin Dies Jr."), chairman of the committee, demanded the suppression of the [American Communist Party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Communist_Party "American Communist Party"). Trotsky intended to use the forum to expose the NKVD's activities against him and his followers.

He made it clear that he also intended to argue against the suppression of the American Communist Party and to use the committee as a platform for a call to transform [World War II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_II "World War II") into a world revolution. Many of his supporters argued against his appearance. When the committee learned the nature of the testimony Trotsky intended to present, it refused to hear him, and he was denied a visa to enter the United States. On hearing about it, the Communist Party of the Soviet Union immediately accused Trotsky of being in the pay of the oil magnates and the [Federal Bureau of Investigation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_Bureau_of_Investigation "Federal Bureau of Investigation").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2003c482_227-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2003c482-227">[217]</a></sup>

### Final months\[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Leon_Trotsky&action=edit&section=37 "Edit section: Final months")\]

After quarreling with Diego Rivera, Trotsky moved to his final residence on Avenida Viena in April 1939.<sup id="cite_ref-228"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-228">[218]</a></sup> On 27 February 1940, Trotsky wrote a document known as "Trotsky's Testament", in which he expressed his final thoughts and feelings for posterity. He was suffering from [high blood pressure](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/High_blood_pressure "High blood pressure"), and feared that he would suffer a [cerebral haemorrhage](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cerebral_haemorrhage "Cerebral haemorrhage"). He would also reiterate his "unshaken faith in a [communist future](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_communism "World communism")".<sup id="cite_ref-Testament_229-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-Testament-229">[219]</a></sup> After forcefully denying Stalin's accusations that he had betrayed the working class, he thanked his friends and above all his wife, Natalia Sedova, for their loyal support:

> In addition to the happiness of being a fighter for the cause of socialism, fate gave me the happiness of being her husband. During the almost forty years of our life together she remained an inexhaustible source of love, magnanimity, and tenderness. She underwent great sufferings, especially in the last period of our lives. But I find some comfort in the fact that she also knew days of happiness. For forty-three years of my conscious life I have remained a revolutionist; for forty-two of them I have fought under the banner of Marxism. If I had to begin all over again I would of course try to avoid this or that mistake, but the main course of my life would remain unchanged. I shall die a proletarian revolutionist, a Marxist, a [dialectical materialist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dialectical_materialist "Dialectical materialist"), and, consequently, an irreconcilable [atheist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atheist "Atheist"). My faith in the communist future of mankind is not less ardent, indeed it is firmer today, than it was in the days of my youth.  
> Natasha has just come up to the window from the courtyard and opened it wider so that the air may enter more freely into my room. I can see the bright green strip of grass beneath the wall, and the clear blue sky above the wall, and sunlight everywhere. Life is beautiful. Let the future generations cleanse it of all [evil](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Evil "Evil"), [oppression](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oppression "Oppression") and [violence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Violence "Violence"), and enjoy it to the full.  
> L. Trotsky  
> 27 February 1940  
> Coyoacán.<sup id="cite_ref-Testament_229-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-Testament-229">[219]</a></sup>

## Assassination\[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Leon_Trotsky&action=edit&section=38 "Edit section: Assassination")\]

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Trotsky_last_office.jpg/220px-Trotsky_last_office.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Trotsky_last_office.jpg)

The study where Leon Trotsky was assassinated with an ice axe on 20 August 1940

After a failed attempt to have Trotsky murdered in March 1939, Stalin assigned the overall organization of implementing the task to the NKVD officer [Pavel Sudoplatov](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pavel_Sudoplatov "Pavel Sudoplatov"), who, in turn, co-opted [Nahum Eitingon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nahum_Eitingon "Nahum Eitingon"). According to Sudoplatov's _[Special Tasks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special_Tasks "Special Tasks")_, the NKVD proceeded to set up three NKVD agent networks to carry out the murder; these three networks were designed to operate entirely autonomously from the NKVD's hitherto-established spy networks in the U.S. and Mexico.<sup id="cite_ref-230"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-230">[220]</a></sup>

On 24 May 1940, Trotsky survived a raid on his villa by armed assassins led by the [NKVD](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NKVD "NKVD") agent [Iosif Grigulevich](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iosif_Grigulevich "Iosif Grigulevich") and Mexican painter [David Alfaro Siqueiros](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Alfaro_Siqueiros "David Alfaro Siqueiros").<sup id="cite_ref-231"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-231">[221]</a></sup> Trotsky's 14-year-old grandson, Vsevolod Platonovich "Esteban" Volkov (7 March 1926 – 16 June 2023), was shot in the foot. A young assistant and bodyguard of Trotsky, [Robert Sheldon Harte](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Sheldon_Harte "Robert Sheldon Harte"), disappeared with the attackers and was later found murdered; it is probable that he was an accomplice who granted them access to the villa.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEService2010485_232-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService2010485-232">[222]</a></sup> Trotsky's other guards fended off the attackers.<sup id="cite_ref-233"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-233">[223]</a></sup> Following the failed assassination attempt, Trotsky wrote an article titled "Stalin Seeks My Death" on 8 June 1940, in which he stated that another assassination attempt was certain.<sup id="cite_ref-234"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-234">[224]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-235"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-235">[225]</a></sup>

On 20 August 1940, Trotsky was attacked in his study by Spanish-born NKVD agent [Ramón Mercader](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ram%C3%B3n_Mercader "Ramón Mercader"), who used an [ice axe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ice_axe "Ice axe")<sup id="cite_ref-236"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-236">[226]</a></sup> as a weapon.<sup id="cite_ref-237"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-237">[227]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-239"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-239">[k]</a></sup> The operation was known within the NKVD as "Operation Utka" (Operation Duck).

A mountaineering ice axe has a narrow end, called the pick, and a flat wide end called the [adze](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adze "Adze"). The adze of the axe wounded Trotsky, fracturing his [parietal bone](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parietal_bone "Parietal bone") and penetrating 7 cm (2.8 in) into his brain.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESoto-Pérez-de-Celis2010_240-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTESoto-P%C3%A9rez-de-Celis2010-240">[229]</a></sup> The blow to his head was bungled and failed to kill Trotsky instantly. Witnesses stated that Trotsky spat on Mercader and began struggling fiercely with him, which resulted in Mercader's hand being broken. Hearing the commotion, Trotsky's bodyguards burst into the room and nearly beat Mercader to death, but Trotsky stopped them, laboriously stating that the assassin should be made to answer questions.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1996466_241-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1996466-241">[230]</a></sup> Trotsky was then taken to a hospital and operated on, surviving for more than a day, yet ultimately dying at the age of 60 on the 21st of August, 1940 from blood loss and shock.<sup id="cite_ref-242"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-242">[231]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESoto-Pérez-de-Celis2010_240-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTESoto-P%C3%A9rez-de-Celis2010-240">[229]</a></sup> Mercader later testified at his trial:

> I laid my raincoat on the table in such a way as to be able to remove the ice axe which was in the pocket. I decided not to miss the wonderful opportunity that presented itself. The moment Trotsky began reading the article, he gave me my chance; I took out the ice axe from the raincoat, gripped it in my hand and, with my eyes closed, dealt him a terrible blow on the head.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1996466_241-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1996466-241">[230]</a></sup>

According to James Cannon, the Trotskyist secretary of the American [Socialist Workers Party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Socialist_Workers_Party_(United_States) "Socialist Workers Party (United States)"), Trotsky's last words were "I will not survive this attack. Stalin has finally accomplished the task he attempted unsuccessfully before."<sup id="cite_ref-243"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-243">[232]</a></sup> Mercader was tried and convicted of the murder and spent the next 20 years in a Mexican prison. Stalin wrote that the assassin of Trotsky was a dangerous Trotskyist. This is why Mercader had no awards initially, though his mother was presented with the [Order of Lenin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Order_of_Lenin "Order of Lenin") for her own part of the operation. Ramón Mercader could not be either assassinated or freed from prison by the Soviets. When he was released from jail in 1960 and arrived in the USSR in 1961, [Leonid Brezhnev](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leonid_Brezhnev "Leonid Brezhnev") signed a sentence to award Mercader the Order of Lenin, the Gold Star, and the title of the [Hero of the Soviet Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hero_of_the_Soviet_Union "Hero of the Soviet Union") "for the special deed". The [KGB](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/KGB "KGB") boss [Alexander Shelepin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_Shelepin "Alexander Shelepin") presented all these awards to Ramón Mercader in person.<sup id="cite_ref-244"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-244">[233]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-245"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-245">[234]</a></sup>

In the aftermath of Trotsky's assassination, an estimated 300,000 people had passed by his funeral casket in Mexico City over several days by 27 August 1940.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENorth2010129_246-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTENorth2010129-246">[235]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-247"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-247">[236]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-248"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-248">[237]</a></sup>

## Personality and characteristics\[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Leon_Trotsky&action=edit&section=39 "Edit section: Personality and characteristics")\]

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Portrait_of_Leon_Trotsky.jpg/220px-Portrait_of_Leon_Trotsky.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Portrait_of_Leon_Trotsky.jpg)

Portrait of Leon Trotsky as Commander of the Red Army, 1920

Trotsky was regarded as an outstanding orator,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEService20091–10_249-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService20091%E2%80%9310-249">[238]</a></sup> preeminent theoretician<sup id="cite_ref-250"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-250">[239]</a></sup> and organiser that, in the view of historian [Michael Kort](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michael_Kort "Michael Kort"), "forged and directed the Red Army".<sup id="cite_ref-251"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-251">[240]</a></sup> He served as one of the original [Politburo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Politburo "Politburo") members in Lenin's government.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1996185_252-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1996185-252">[241]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-253"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-253">[242]</a></sup> Biographer [Isaac Deutscher](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isaac_Deutscher "Isaac Deutscher") considered him to be the "prompter of \[the\] [planned economy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Planned_economy "Planned economy") and industrialization" during the early years of the Soviet Union.<sup id="cite_ref-254"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-254">[243]</a></sup> Historian [Laura Engelstein](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Laura_Engelstein "Laura Engelstein") judged Trotsky to be personally fastidious, but possessing the qualities of vanity and volatility which were not shared with Lenin. Engelstein also described him as talented and dynamic, "but only a [second in command](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_in_command "Second in command")".<sup id="cite_ref-255"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-255">[244]</a></sup>

Political theorist [Ernest Mandel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ernest_Mandel "Ernest Mandel") summarised the dominant image of Trotsky as "self-confident",<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMandel1995156_256-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMandel1995156-256">[245]</a></sup> "unshakeable in the conviction of his historic mission",<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMandel1995155–156_257-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMandel1995155%E2%80%93156-257">[246]</a></sup> "strict with others and himself"<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMandel1995165–166_258-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMandel1995165%E2%80%93166-258">[247]</a></sup> and "indifferent to material privileges and to the small joys and sorrows of life".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMandel1995165–166_258-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMandel1995165%E2%80%93166-258">[247]</a></sup> Mandel argued this image reflected "certain aspects of Trotsky's personality, strengths and weaknesses".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMandel1995165–166_258-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMandel1995165%E2%80%93166-258">[247]</a></sup>

Historian [Simon Sebag Montefiore](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Simon_Sebag_Montefiore "Simon Sebag Montefiore") described Trotsky as the "genius of the revolution"<sup id="cite_ref-259"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-259">[248]</a></sup> and biographer [Dmitri Volkogonov](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dmitri_Volkogonov "Dmitri Volkogonov") characterised him as a "vivid, complex, multi-faceted personality in the gallery of world figures" who was remembered "with hatred and respect, anger and admiration" decades after his assassination in Mexico.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1996xxxi_260-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1996xxxi-260">[249]</a></sup> Volkogonov also found Trotsky to be a constant "spectre" for Stalin, after his exile, and also wrote that he was "of a different calibre intellectually, with his grasp of organization and his talents as a speaker and writer". Volkogonov considered Trotsky "far superior" to figures such as [Molotov](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vyacheslav_Molotov "Vyacheslav Molotov"), [Kaganovich](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lazar_Kaganovich "Lazar Kaganovich"), [Khrushchev](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khrushchev "Khrushchev"), [Zhdanov](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zhdanov "Zhdanov") and "also superior to Stalin and Stalin knew it".<sup id="cite_ref-261"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-261">[250]</a></sup>

Biographer [Robert Service](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Service_(historian) "Robert Service (historian)") commented that he was a "volatile and untrustworthy",<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEService20091–10_249-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService20091%E2%80%9310-249">[238]</a></sup> "arrogant individual"<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEService20091–10_249-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService20091%E2%80%9310-249">[238]</a></sup> that impressed supporters even during the periods of "personal adversity in the 1920s and 1930s"<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEService20091–10_249-3"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService20091%E2%80%9310-249">[238]</a></sup> but failed to "coax and encourage them to the full".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEService20091–10_249-4"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService20091%E2%80%9310-249">[238]</a></sup> Service stated that Trotsky gave the "minimum time to the Jewish question" and believed that "he ceased to be a Jew in any important sense because Marxism had burned out the fortuitous residues of his origins".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEService2009200–201_262-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService2009200%E2%80%93201-262">[251]</a></sup>

Political scientist August Nimtz regarded Trotsky to have had better foresight than Marxist and some non-Marxist intellectual observers with his work [_The Revolution Betrayed: What Is the Soviet Union and Where Is It Going?_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Revolution_Betrayed "The Revolution Betrayed") (1936). Trotsky argued that the Stalinist regime was an "ephemeral phenomenon" and Nimtz believed this had later been proven with the [Soviet collapse after 1989](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union "Dissolution of the Soviet Union").<sup id="cite_ref-263"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-263">[252]</a></sup> Other scholars have similarly described Trotsky as having a prescient judgement of events such as the rise of [Nazi Germany](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazi_Germany "Nazi Germany") and [The Spanish Civil War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Spanish_Civil_War "The Spanish Civil War") through his political writings and levels of military accuracy.<sup id="cite_ref-264"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-264">[253]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-265"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-265">[254]</a></sup> Deutscher also referenced his "uncanny clear sightedness" in predicting the emergence of a single dictator who would "substitute himself" for the [Central Committee](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Committee_of_the_Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union "Central Committee of the Communist Party of the Soviet Union"), the party and the working class.<sup id="cite_ref-266"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-266">[255]</a></sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Trotsky_at_Copenhagen.jpg/300px-Trotsky_at_Copenhagen.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Trotsky_at_Copenhagen.jpg)

Trotsky delivering a speech at the [University of Copenhagen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_Copenhagen "University of Copenhagen") in 1932

Trotsky was a [Marxist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marxist "Marxist") [intellectual](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intellectual "Intellectual").<sup id="cite_ref-267"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-267">[256]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-268"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-268">[257]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-269"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-269">[258]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-270"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-270">[259]</a></sup> Russian historian Vladimir Buldakov considered Trotsky, in some respect, a "typical representative" of "Russia's radical [intelligentsia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intelligentsia "Intelligentsia")" who had "elements of bourgeois origin".<sup id="cite_ref-271"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-271">[260]</a></sup> He had a diverse and profound range of interests which exceeded that of other Bolshevik theoreticians such as [Nikolai Bukharin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nikolai_Bukharin "Nikolai Bukharin").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMandel1995168–169_272-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMandel1995168%E2%80%93169-272">[261]</a></sup> He also had a notable interest in [literature](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Literature_and_Revolution "Literature and Revolution") and wrote on "everyday life and cultural progress as well as on the more customary Marxism of the day".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEService20091–10_249-5"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService20091%E2%80%9310-249">[238]</a></sup> Trotsky and his second wife, [Natalia Sedova](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natalia_Sedova "Natalia Sedova") enjoyed Viennese galleries and made frequent visits to museums such as the [Louvre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louvre "Louvre") and the [Tate Gallery](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tate_Gallery "Tate Gallery") across Europe to view specific art collections.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2003a152_273-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2003a152-273">[262]</a></sup> He also retained a personal interest in [science](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Science "Science") which stemmed from his youth when he considered studying mathematics and physics at the New Russian University in Odessa.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEService2009327_274-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService2009327-274">[263]</a></sup>

His personal secretary and later a historian of mathematical logic, [Jean van Heijenoort](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jean_van_Heijenoort "Jean van Heijenoort"), considered him to be amicable, inquisitive and occasionally charming with new acquaintances during his final years in Mexico.<sup id="cite_ref-275"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-275">[264]</a></sup> Old Bolshevik [Anatoly Lunacharsky](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anatoly_Lunacharsky "Anatoly Lunacharsky") viewed Trotsky as the best prepared among the [Social-Democratic leaders](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Social_Democratic_Labour_Party "Russian Social Democratic Labour Party") during the [1905–07 revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Revolution_of_1905 "Russian Revolution of 1905") and stated that he "emerged from the revolution having acquired an enormous degree of popularity, whereas neither Lenin nor Martov had effectively gained any at all".<sup id="cite_ref-276"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-276">[265]</a></sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Leon_Trotsky_with_his_second_wife_in_1932.jpg/300px-Leon_Trotsky_with_his_second_wife_in_1932.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Leon_Trotsky_with_his_second_wife_in_1932.jpg)

Trotsky with his second wife in 1932

His arch enemy, Stalin, even read and sometimes appreciated a great deal of his writings.<sup id="cite_ref-277"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-277">[266]</a></sup> According to Rubenstein, Stalin had even acknowledged that "after Lenin, Trotsky was the most [popular](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Popularity "Popularity") figure in the country" at the end of the Civil War.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERubenstein2011127_159-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTERubenstein2011127-159">[153]</a></sup> He also recognized the prominent role of Trotsky during the October revolution in the 1917 [Pravda](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pravda "Pravda") editorial. Stalin himself wrote: "All practical work in connection with the organization of the uprising was done under the immediate direction of Comrade Trotsky, the president of the Petrograd Soviet".<sup id="cite_ref-278"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-278">[267]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-279"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-279">[268]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-280"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-280">[269]</a></sup>

Upon his exile in 1929, eighteen of his close relatives remained in the Soviet Union and all were subjected to repressive measures with seven of his family members including his son [Sergei Sedov](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sergei_Sedov "Sergei Sedov"), sister [Olga Kameneva](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Olga_Kameneva "Olga Kameneva") and brother Aleksandr Bronstein having been shot.<sup id="cite_ref-281"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-281">[270]</a></sup> He spoke several European languages "with a markedly Russian accent"<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEService2009200_282-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService2009200-282">[271]</a></sup> and identified as a cosmopolitan and internationalist.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEService2009200–205_283-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService2009200%E2%80%93205-283">[272]</a></sup> In the course of his life, Trotsky wrote about 30,000 documents, most of which are contained in various archives.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1996xxx_284-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1996xxx-284">[273]</a></sup> Deutscher stated that Trotsky wrote most of the [Soviet's](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saint_Petersburg_Soviet "Saint Petersburg Soviet") manifestos and resolutions, edited its Izvestia newspaper and also composed the oath of loyalty for the Red Army.<sup id="cite_ref-285"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-285">[274]</a></sup> According to Mandel, Trotsky wrote the Zimmerwald Manifesto for the [Zimmerwald Conference](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zimmerwald_Conference "Zimmerwald Conference") because he was radically opposed to [World War I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I "World War I") and drafted the Appeal for the Convocation of the [First Comintern Congress](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1st_Congress_of_the_Comintern "1st Congress of the Comintern") due to his active involvement with the [Third International](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Third_International "Third International").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMandel199522_286-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMandel199522-286">[275]</a></sup> He also served as a member of the [Executive Committee of the Communist International](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Executive_Committee_of_the_Communist_International "Executive Committee of the Communist International") for the initial Congress sessions.<sup id="cite_ref-287"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-287">[276]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-288"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-288">[277]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMandel199522_286-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMandel199522-286">[275]</a></sup>

Aside from his interest in political activism, Trotsky also worked as a [statistician](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statistician "Statistician") and a journalist.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERenton20046_289-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTERenton20046-289">[278]</a></sup> Trotsky stated that he worked for three newspapers and oversaw the _"Russian Gazette"_ with [Alexander Parvus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_Parvus "Alexander Parvus"). He claimed that the circulation under his tenure had increased from 30,000 to 500,000.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEService201094_290-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService201094-290">[279]</a></sup> However, historians Anthony Heywood and Jonathan Smele believe this was an exaggerated claim and cited circulation figures from the editors of Trotsky's collected works that the figures had in fact increased to 100,000 which they still regarded as impressive and comparatively ahead of Lenin's _[New Life](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Novaya_Zhizn "Novaya Zhizn")_ newspaper by 20,000.<sup id="cite_ref-291"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-291">[280]</a></sup>

## Political stature and conflicts with Stalin\[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Leon_Trotsky&action=edit&section=40 "Edit section: Political stature and conflicts with Stalin")\]

> Had Trotsky won the struggle to succeed Lenin, the character of the Soviet regime would almost certainly have been substantially different, particularly in [foreign policy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Foreign_policy "Foreign policy"), [cultural policy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cultural_policy "Cultural policy"), and the extent of terroristic [repression](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Political_repression "Political repression"). Trotsky's failure, however, seems to have been almost inevitable, considering his own qualities and the conditions of authoritarian rule by the Communist Party organization.

—Historian Robert Vincent Daniels, 1993<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDaniels1993945–946_292-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDaniels1993945%E2%80%93946-292">[281]</a></sup>

Historian [Robert Vincent Daniels](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Vincent_Daniels "Robert Vincent Daniels") expressed the view that Trotsky was "undoubtedly the most brilliant [intellect](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intellect "Intellect") brought to prominence by the [Russian Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Revolution "Russian Revolution"), outdistancing Lenin and other theoreticians both in the range of his interests and in the imaginativeness of his perceptions". Yet, he emphasised his personal arrogance as an underlying weakness which antagonised other members of the communist movement. Daniels also argued that had Trotsky assumed the role of [Lenin's successor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lenin%27s_Testament "Lenin's Testament") then he would have presided over an [alternate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Counterfactual_history "Counterfactual history") Soviet Union markedly distinct from Stalin's regime.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDaniels1993945–946_292-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDaniels1993945%E2%80%93946-292">[281]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-293"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-293">[282]</a></sup>

Contrarily, Service asserted that the succession of Trotsky would have resulted in a similar [totalitarian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Totalitarian "Totalitarian") dictatorship akin to Stalin's rule and increased the likelihood of conflict across the European continent.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEService20103_294-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService20103-294">[283]</a></sup> Although, historian [Sheila Fitzpatrick](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sheila_Fitzpatrick "Sheila Fitzpatrick") found it implausible that Trotsky like Stalin would have launched an [anti-semitic campaign](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-cosmopolitan_campaign "Anti-cosmopolitan campaign") after [World War II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_II "World War II") or initiated the [Great Purge](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Purge "Great Purge"). Rather, she suggested Trotsky would presumably have provided good leadership during the Second World War but may have struggled to maintain party cohesion as seen during the succession struggle after 1924.<sup id="cite_ref-295"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-295">[284]</a></sup> Political theorist [David North](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_North_(socialist) "David North (socialist)") argued that Trotsky's military policies would have averted the dismantlement of Soviet defenses alongside the [high levels of human casualties](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_II_casualties_of_the_Soviet_Union "World War II casualties of the Soviet Union") associated with [Operation Barbarossa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Barbarossa "Operation Barbarossa") and the [Second World War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_World_War "Second World War").<sup id="cite_ref-296"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-296">[285]</a></sup> Biographer Geoffrey Swain believed that the Soviet Union under the leadership of Trotsky would have been far more [technocratic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Technocratic "Technocratic") due to his reliance on "bourgeois experts" in the [planning process](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economic_planning "Economic planning").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESwain2014a118_297-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTESwain2014a118-297">[286]</a></sup> Other scholars have pointed to the fact that Trotsky opposed the policy of forced collectivisation under Stalin and favoured a [voluntary](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Volunteering "Volunteering"), gradual approach towards [agricultural production](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Collective_farming "Collective farming") as an area of differentiation.<sup id="cite_ref-298"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-298">[287]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-299"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-299">[288]</a></sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/SovietDelegatesAtBrestLitovsk.jpg/350px-SovietDelegatesAtBrestLitovsk.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:SovietDelegatesAtBrestLitovsk.jpg)

Trotsky as [People's Commissar for Foreign Affairs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Minister_of_Foreign_Affairs_(Russia)#Russian_SFSR_(1917%E2%80%931991) "Minister of Foreign Affairs (Russia)") with the Soviet delegation at Brest-Litovsk, 1917

His enmity with Stalin developed during the Civil War with the latter's disregard of military specialists whom Trotsky considered indispensable for the success of the Red Army. In [Tsaritsyn](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tsaritsyn "Tsaritsyn"), Stalin ordered the imprisonment of several specialists on a [barge](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barge "Barge") in the [Volga](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Volga "Volga") river and oversaw the sinking of the floating prison in which the officers perished.<sup id="cite_ref-300"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-300">[289]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-301"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-301">[290]</a></sup> Another instance was when Stalin disobeyed Trotsky's order to march on Warsaw which contributed to the defeat of the Red Army at the [Battle of Warsaw](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Warsaw_(1920) "Battle of Warsaw (1920)") in 1920.<sup id="cite_ref-302"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-302">[291]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-303"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-303">[292]</a></sup> Bazhanov also claimed that Stalin's antagonism towards Trotsky stemmed from the fact that he was Jewish and that the former would refuse to obey military orders during the Russian Civil War.<sup id="cite_ref-304"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-304">[293]</a></sup> According to Rogovin, Trotsky received hundreds of letters reporting the use of [anti-semitic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-semitic "Anti-semitic") methods during the inter-party struggle between Stalin and the United Opposition.<sup id="cite_ref-305"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-305">[294]</a></sup> Similar disputes extended to cultural matters in which Trotsky defended intellectual autonomy in regards to literary movements as well scientific theories such as [Freudian psychoanalytic theory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freud%27s_psychoanalytic_theories "Freud's psychoanalytic theories") and [Einstein](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Einstein "Einstein")’s [theory of relativity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theory_of_relativity "Theory of relativity") during the succession period. However, these theories were increasingly marginalised during the Stalin era.<sup id="cite_ref-306"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-306">[295]</a></sup>

Trotsky lacked the political acumen to succeed against Stalin's machinations.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMccauley201459_307-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMccauley201459-307">[296]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hitler_and_Stalin_:_parallel_lives_156-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-Hitler_and_Stalin_:_parallel_lives-156">[150]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-308"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-308">[297]</a></sup> Lenin had encouraged Trotsky, in his absence, to challenge Stalin at the [Twelfth Party Congress](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/12th_Congress_of_the_Russian_Communist_Party_(Bolsheviks) "12th Congress of the Russian Communist Party (Bolsheviks)") over the Georgian Affair but the latter relented.<sup id="cite_ref-309"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-309">[298]</a></sup> Historian [Peter Kenez](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peter_Kenez "Peter Kenez") believed that Trotsky could probably have removed Stalin with the use of Lenin's testament but he "stupidly" acquiesced to the collective decision not to publish the document.<sup id="cite_ref-310"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-310">[299]</a></sup> Historian [Martin McCauley](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Martin_McCauley_(historian) "Martin McCauley (historian)") commented that Trotsky "displayed a lamentable lack of political judgement" on multiple occasions such as declining Lenin's proposal to become [deputy chairman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deputy_Premier_of_the_Soviet_Union "Deputy Premier of the Soviet Union") of Sovnarkom, failing to build a power base before forming a bloc with Lenin against the [Orgburo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orgburo "Orgburo") and not immediately recognising that a [triumvirate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Triumvirate "Triumvirate") had been established to prevent his succession.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMccauley201459_307-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMccauley201459-307">[296]</a></sup> Rubenstein differed in his interpretation and attributed Trotsky's decision to decline Lenin's proposal because he believed the position had "little authority of its own" and overlapped with other government and party officials.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERubenstein2011127_159-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTERubenstein2011127-159">[153]</a></sup> Deutscher believed he had underestimated Stalin's cunning, ruthlessness and tenacity on several occasions.<sup id="cite_ref-311"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-311">[300]</a></sup> Political scientist Richard B.Day argued that it was more probable that Trotsky's interest in building [socialism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Socialism "Socialism") outweighted his desire for personal [power](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Power_(social_and_political) "Power (social and political)").<sup id="cite_ref-312"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-312">[301]</a></sup>

> “With all the greater frankness can I state how, in my view, the Soviet government should act in case of a fascist upheaval in Germany. In their place, I would, at the very moment of receiving telegraphic news of this event, sign a mobilisation order calling up several age groups. In the face of a mortal enemy, when the logic of the situation points to inevitable war, it would be irresponsible and unpardonable to give that enemy time to establish himself, to consolidate his positions, to conclude alliances… and to work out the plan to attack..”

Trotsky describing the military measures he would have taken in place of Stalin to counter the rise of [Nazi Germany](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazi_Germany "Nazi Germany") in 1932.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2015a1192–1193_313-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2015a1192%E2%80%931193-313">[302]</a></sup>

Historian [Orlando Figes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orlando_Figes "Orlando Figes") noted that Trotsky never held a party post and rarely attended party meetings despite serving as a member of the Politburo. Figes also described him as having "too many characteristics that made it extraordinarily hard to work collectively with him". <sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFiges2017794_314-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFiges2017794-314">[303]</a></sup> Biographer [Joshua Rubenstein](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joshua_Rubenstein "Joshua Rubenstein") regarded Trotsky's position among the Soviet elites as largely dependent on Lenin.
