Rubenstein also added that he had an image of an outsider within party circles as he had previously been an "outspoken critic of Lenin".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERubenstein2011126_315-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTERubenstein2011126-315">[304]</a></sup> Conversely, Volkongov stated that Trotsky had the support of many party [intellectuals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intellectual "Intellectual") but this was overshadowed by the huge apparatus which included the GPU and the party cadres who were at the disposal of Stalin.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1996284_316-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1996284-316">[305]</a></sup> Historian [Paul Dukes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Dukes_(historian) "Paul Dukes (historian)") considered it a debatable notion that his personal "sophistication" as a political figure led to "his defeat in the great struggle of 1923 and after". He also reached the view that Trotsky did not share Stalin's understanding of the party in which "fewer than 10 percent of its members were fully [literate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Literate "Literate")" and this was in spite of the fact that Stalin "was a man of narrower outlook in virtually every respect".<sup id="cite_ref-The_Trotsky_reappraisal_317-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-The_Trotsky_reappraisal-317">[306]</a></sup>

Trotsky himself ascribed his political defeat to external, objective conditions rather than the individual qualities of Stalin. He specifically argued that the failed series of international insurrections as seen in [Bulgaria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/September_Uprising "September Uprising") in 1923 and [China](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shanghai_massacre "Shanghai massacre") in 1927 had diminished the prospect of [world socialism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_socialism "World socialism") and demoralised the Russian working class which in turn strengthened the growth of an internal, Soviet bureaucracy.<sup id="cite_ref-318"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-318">[307]</a></sup> Russian historian [Vadim Rogovin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vadim_Rogovin "Vadim Rogovin") also remarked that Trotsky, in the 1930s, did not abandon hope for the spread of the revolution. Rogovin argued that Trotsky's prognosis of world events was plausible as a majority of European countries such as [Germany](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Germany "Germany"), [France](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/France "France"), and especially [Spain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spain "Spain"), "went through a period of revolutionary crisis".<sup id="cite_ref-319"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-319">[308]</a></sup> Although, Daniels contended that Trotsky would have in reality been no more prepared than other Bolshevik figures to risk [war](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/War "War") or the loss of [trade](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trade "Trade") opportunities despite his support for world revolution.<sup id="cite_ref-Yale_University_Press_320-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-Yale_University_Press-320">[309]</a></sup>

## Relations with Lenin\[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Leon_Trotsky&action=edit&section=41 "Edit section: Relations with Lenin")\]

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/19191107-lenin_second_anniversary_october_revolution_moscow.jpg/220px-19191107-lenin_second_anniversary_october_revolution_moscow.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:19191107-lenin_second_anniversary_october_revolution_moscow.jpg)

Celebration of the second anniversary of the October Revolution in Moscow, 1919. One of the photos of which the image of Trotsky was erased, along with those of [Lev Kamenev](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lev_Kamenev "Lev Kamenev") and [Artemic Khalatov](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artemic_Khalatov "Artemic Khalatov").

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Lenin_Speech_in_May_1920.png/220px-Lenin_Speech_in_May_1920.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Lenin_Speech_in_May_1920.png)

Lenin delivering a speech to a crowd in Moscow Square, with [Trotsky](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trotsky "Trotsky") and [Kamenev](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kamenev "Kamenev") in the background, May 1920.

His relations with Lenin have been a source of intense historical debate.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESwain2014b1–10North201052–90_321-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTESwain2014b1%E2%80%9310North201052%E2%80%9390-321">[310]</a></sup> Historian [Paul Le Blanc](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Le_Blanc_(historian) "Paul Le Blanc (historian)") and philosopher [Michael Lowy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michael_Lowy "Michael Lowy") described Lenin and Trotsky as the "widely leading figures in the Russia's Bolshevik Revolution of 1917 as well as in the final years of the rising world communist movement". They characterized Lenin and Trotsky as "fierce adversaries" during the early years of the Russian socialist movement but described the duo as having reached a convergence and a substantial agreement in 1917 before colliding their efforts to achieve the October Revolution. They also highlighted the mutual appreciation and respect between Lenin and Trotsky with the former seeking to work closely with Trotsky on the [Iskra](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iskra "Iskra") newspaper, prior to their polemical disagreements, and Lenin acknowledging that his theory on permanent revolution "happened to be right" after 1917.<sup id="cite_ref-Palgrave_Handbook_322-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-Palgrave_Handbook-322">[311]</a></sup>

However, Swain viewed the notion that Trotsky was Lenin's natural heir a myth and cited several scholars such as Erik Van Rees, James White and Richard B.Day who Swain claimed had challenged the traditional characterization of their relationship.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESwain2014b1–10_323-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTESwain2014b1%E2%80%9310-323">[312]</a></sup> North specifically rejected this position and argued Swain sought to discredit historical works appreciative of Trotsky. North continued to argue that Swain gave an insufficient consideration of the "complex historical, political, social and theoretical issues that arise in any serious study of the Lenin-Trotsky relationship". He also asserted that Swain had distorted and misrepresented the positions of the cited scholars.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENorth201052–90_324-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTENorth201052%E2%80%9390-324">[313]</a></sup> Le Blanc also disputed Swain's representation of Trotsky and referenced various historians which included [E.H. Carr](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/E.H._Carr "E.H. Carr"), [Isaac Deutscher](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isaac_Deutscher "Isaac Deutscher"), [Moshe Lewin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moshe_Lewin "Moshe Lewin"), [Ronald Suny](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ronald_Suny "Ronald Suny") and [W. Bruce Lincoln](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/W._Bruce_Lincoln "W. Bruce Lincoln") across different generations. According to Le Blanc, these historians on balance had tilted "toward the view that Lenin's desired "heir" was collective responsibility in which Trotsky placed an important role and within which Stalin would be dramatically demoted (if not removed)".<sup id="cite_ref-325"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-325">[314]</a></sup> Similarly, historian [Roy Medvedev](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roy_Medvedev "Roy Medvedev") noted the close association of Trotsky and Lenin in the Soviet republic throughout the period of 1921–24. Medvedev mentioned a number of public commendations such as "greetings in honour of comrades Lenin and Trotsky were announced at many [rallies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Political_demonstration "Political demonstration") and meetings, and [portraits](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Portraits "Portraits") of Lenin and Trotsky hung on the walls of many Soviet and party institutions".<sup id="cite_ref-326"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-326">[315]</a></sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Lenin_in_1920_%28cropped%29.jpg/174px-Lenin_in_1920_%28cropped%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Lenin_in_1920_(cropped).jpg)

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Trotsky_Profile.jpg/160px-Trotsky_Profile.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Trotsky_Profile.jpg)

Initially, Lenin turned down the leading position of [Chairman of the Council of People's Commissars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chairman_of_the_Council_of_People%27s_Commissars "Chairman of the Council of People's Commissars") when the Bolsheviks formed a new government, after the [October Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/October_Revolution "October Revolution") in 1917, and suggested Trotsky for the position. However, Trotsky refused the position and other Bolsheviks insisted that Lenin assume principal responsibility which thereafter resulted in Lenin eventually accepting the role of chairman.<sup id="cite_ref-327"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-327">[316]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-328"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-328">[317]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-329"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-329">[318]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEService2010191_330-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService2010191-330">[319]</a></sup> On a separate occasion, Lenin expressed hostility to the early attempts by the triumvirate to remove Trotsky from the leadership. In a 1922 memo written to Kamenev, he chastised the efforts by the Central Committee to "throw Trotsky overboard" as the "height of stupidity. If you do not consider me already hopelessly foolish, how can you think of that ?".<sup id="cite_ref-331"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-331">[320]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-332"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-332">[321]</a></sup> In his last testament, Lenin urged the wider party circles to not use and hold Trotsky's [non-Bolshevik](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mezhraiontsy "Mezhraiontsy") past against him.<sup id="cite_ref-333"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-333">[322]</a></sup>

Soviet writer [Maxim Gorky](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maxim_Gorky "Maxim Gorky") recollected Lenin in the first version of his sketch, _V.I. Lenin_, dismissing rumours of an alleged political difference between himself and Trotsky with the words: "There are many lies, and it seems, particularly many lies about me and Trotsky". Gorky also stated that Lenin made an approving assessment of Trotsky due to his military organisation of the army in a single year.<sup id="cite_ref-334"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-334">[323]</a></sup> In the view of Lenin's wife, [Nadezhda Krupskaya](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nadezhda_Krupskaya "Nadezhda Krupskaya"), Lenin was "pleased with the definite manner" of Trotsky's theoretical comprehension of diverging Russian revolutionary movements during their first meeting in 1902. She similarly expressed this view in a personal note after Lenin's death that her husband's attitude towards Trotsky had "not changed until his death" since their initial meeting in London.<sup id="cite_ref-Palgrave_Handbook_322-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-Palgrave_Handbook-322">[311]</a></sup> In his final months, Lenin read several of Trotsky's works among a wider collection of books which interested him. Lenin read _Problems of Everyday Life_ in the last month of his life and instructed Krupskaya to read him a passage from another of Trotsky's books that characterised Marxism and Leninism. Lenin also read Trotsky's pamphlet, _[The New Course](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Course_(Trotsky_book) "New Course (Trotsky book)")_, on the day prior to his death.<sup id="cite_ref-335"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-335">[324]</a></sup> According to Stalin's secretary, [Boris Bazhanov](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boris_Bazhanov "Boris Bazhanov"), Lenin "in general leaned towards a [collegial leadership](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Collective_leadership_in_the_Soviet_Union "Collective leadership in the Soviet Union"), with Trotsky in the first position".<sup id="cite_ref-336"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-336">[325]</a></sup>

### Lenin's succession\[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Leon_Trotsky&action=edit&section=42 "Edit section: Lenin's succession")\]

> Comrade Trotsky, on the other hand, as his struggle against the C.C. on the question of the People's Commissariat of Communications has already proved, is distinguished not only by outstanding ability. He is personally perhaps the most capable man in the present C.C., but he has displayed excessive self-assurance and shown excessive preoccupation with the purely administrative side of the work.

—Lenin's testament; 1923<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewin200580_337-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewin200580-337">[326]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-338"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-338">[327]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-339"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-339">[328]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-340"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-340">[329]</a></sup> Most historians consider the document to be an accurate reflection of Lenin's views.<sup id="cite_ref-341"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-341">[330]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-342"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-342">[331]</a></sup>

Trotsky was generally viewed as Lenin's choice as a successor in 1923.<sup id="cite_ref-343"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-343">[332]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-344"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-344">[333]</a></sup> He had been nominated to be Lenin's deputy in 1922 and 1923 as well as expected to assume responsibility over the [Council of National Economy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supreme_Soviet_of_the_National_Economy "Supreme Soviet of the National Economy") or [Gosplan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gosplan "Gosplan").<sup id="cite_ref-345"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-345">[334]</a></sup> Lenin and Trotsky were also the only Soviet leaders elected honorary presidents of the [Communist International](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communist_International "Communist International").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2015a605_346-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2015a605-346">[335]</a></sup> Prior to the introduction of the factional [ban in 1921](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ban_on_factions_in_the_Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union "Ban on factions in the Communist Party of the Soviet Union"), due to intra-party controversies and the wider conflict of the Civil War, Trotsky had a considerable following among the party activists and members of the Central Committee against the narrow majority supporting Lenin. His supporters also controlled the newly established [Orgburo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orgburo "Orgburo") and the [Party Secretariat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Secretariat_of_the_Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union "Secretariat of the Communist Party of the Soviet Union") before the appointment of Stalin as General Secretary.<sup id="cite_ref-347"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-347">[336]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-348"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-348">[337]</a></sup> According to Mccauley, Lenin had revealed that he planned to retire to the Central Committee and made an arrangement for Trotsky to speak on his behalf as his natural successor which in turn triggered the formation of the troika.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMccauley201452_349-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMccauley201452-349">[338]</a></sup> Forges drew focus to the increasing alignment between Lenin and Trotsky in 1923. He cited Lenin's testament which was critical of Stalin and the bureaucracy along with their shared position on [foreign trade](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Foreign_trade_of_the_Soviet_Union "Foreign trade of the Soviet Union"), party reform and the [Georgian affair](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Georgian_affair "Georgian affair").<sup id="cite_ref-350"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-350">[339]</a></sup>

Rogovin interpreted Lenin's proposal to the Politburo that Trotsky be confirmed as the "[First Deputy Chairman of the Council of the Sovnarkom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Deputy_Premier_of_the_Soviet_Union "First Deputy Premier of the Soviet Union")" as signifying that he was entrusted "with the highest government post" and he argued that this was also considerable given Lenin's illness at the time. Rogovin also referenced a previous proposal by Lenin in 1917 to appoint Trotsky with another senior position as [People's Commissar of Internal Affairs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/People%27s_Commissar_of_Internal_Affairs "People's Commissar of Internal Affairs").<sup id="cite_ref-351"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-351">[340]</a></sup> Yet, historian [Richard Pipes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_Pipes "Richard Pipes") dismissed the view that Trotsky was Lenin's successor due to his proposed and joint appointment as [deputy chairman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deputy_Premier_of_the_Soviet_Union "Deputy Premier of the Soviet Union") with Kamenev in 1922. Pipes attributed this overstated claim to Trotsky's supporters and explained that he had in fact been reprimanded by the party for "categorically refusing" the post.<sup id="cite_ref-352"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-352">[341]</a></sup> Conversely, Medvedev stated that Trotsky "undoubtedly would have been first among Lenin's deputies" given his [authority](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authority "Authority") in 1922 and noted that Kamenev lacked any personal desire to become Chairman upon Lenin's death.<sup id="cite_ref-353"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-353">[342]</a></sup>

[Slavic studies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Slavic_studies "Slavic studies") scholar Derek Watson presumed that Trotsky would have been the first vice-chairman of an additional [RSFSR](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/RSFSR "RSFSR") body working alongside the other deputies.<sup id="cite_ref-354"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-354">[343]</a></sup> Deutscher argued that had Trotsky assumed the post of deputy, then it would have been difficult for [Rykov](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexei_Rykov "Alexei Rykov") to have been promoted above him as chairman after Lenin's death in 1924.<sup id="cite_ref-355"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-355">[344]</a></sup> Polish historian [Marian Kamil Dziewanowski](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marian_Kamil_Dziewanowski "Marian Kamil Dziewanowski") also echoed these views and argued that had Trotsky accepted the post of vice-chairman then his prestige and power would have been strengthened as a counter-weight to Stalin's growing influence. Dziewanowski expressed the view that Trotsky as vice-chairman would have been a natural successor to Lenin as [Chairman of the Soviet Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chairman_of_the_Council_of_People%27s_Commissars_of_the_Soviet_Union "Chairman of the Council of People's Commissars of the Soviet Union"). However, his rejection of the position enabled Stalin to place Rykov as Lenin's successor and serve as a key ally in the Politburo against Trotsky.<sup id="cite_ref-356"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-356">[345]</a></sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Lenin_and_Trotsky.jpg/400px-Lenin_and_Trotsky.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Lenin_and_Trotsky.jpg)

Russian [peasants](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peasants "Peasants") holding [banners](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Banners "Banners") of Lenin (left), [Marx](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marx "Marx") (centre) and Trotsky (right) in early [Soviet Russia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Russia "Soviet Russia").

Similarly, Soviet historian Victor Danilov believed that Lenin's proposed appointment of Trotsky as deputy "would have made him [in effect Lenin's successor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Order_of_succession "Order of succession")". Danilov also cited Politburo Secretary Bazhanov's notes of a concluding speech delivered by Trotsky in 1923 to the wider party membership. Trotsky explained his decision to decline the proposed position of Lenin's chief deputy due to concerns about his "Jewish origins" which could accentuate anti-semitic attitudes towards the Soviet Union.<sup id="cite_ref-357"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-357">[346]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-358"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-358">[347]</a></sup> Mccauley stated that Trotsky would "almost certainly" have become the successor had Lenin succumbed to his first stroke in 1922.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMccauley201451_359-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMccauley201451-359">[348]</a></sup> Deutscher noted that Zinoviev had been Lenin's closest discipline rather than Trotsky between 1907 and 1917. However, Zinoviev's opposition to the October revolution had strained his relations with Lenin.<sup id="cite_ref-360"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-360">[349]</a></sup>

Opponents such as [Winston Churchill](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Winston_Churchill "Winston Churchill") even argued that "Lenin \[had\] indeed regarded Trotsky as his political heir" and sought to protect him before his passing in 1924.<sup id="cite_ref-361"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-361">[350]</a></sup> Zinoviev and Kamenev also viewed Trotsky as Lenin's most likely successor and sided with Stalin out of fear that Trotsky would remove them from the party leadership.<sup id="cite_ref-362"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-362">[351]</a></sup> However, his chief adversary Stalin, strongly denied claims that Trotsky was the succeeding chairman following Lenin's illness. He pointed out that Trotsky was expected to serve as one of several deputy chairmen under Lenin which included Kamenev, Rykov and [Tsiurupa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_Tsiurupa "Alexander Tsiurupa"). Although, he did reference a written document signed by Lenin in 1922 which assigned Trotsky and Kamenev different areas of focus as deputy chairmen. Lenin's authorised document proposed Trotsky as deputy chairman of the Council of Commissars rather than Kamenev who was intended to serve only as a deputy chairman of the [Labour Defence Council](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Council_of_Labor_and_Defense "Council of Labor and Defense").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKosheleva1995b80–90_363-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKosheleva1995b80%E2%80%9390-363">[352]</a></sup> On Lenin's initiative, Stalin requested the Central Committee that Trotsky be appointed deputy chairman and [Chairman of Gosplan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gosplan "Gosplan") in January 1923 but he refused the position.<sup id="cite_ref-364"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-364">[353]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-365"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-365">[354]</a></sup> In his autobiography, _[My Life](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/My_Life_(Trotsky) "My Life (Trotsky)")_, Trotsky maintained that Lenin had intended for him to be his successor as Chairman of the Soviet Union with his proposed appointment as deputy. He explained that this process would have begun after their alliance in 1923 with the formation of a [commission](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Control_Commission_of_the_Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union "Central Control Commission of the Communist Party of the Soviet Union") to mitigate the growth of the [state bureaucracy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bureaucracy "Bureaucracy") which in turn would have facilitated the conditions for his succession in the party.<sup id="cite_ref-366"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-366">[355]</a></sup>

## Legacy\[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Leon_Trotsky&action=edit&section=43 "Edit section: Legacy")\]

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Trotsky_grave.jpg/170px-Trotsky_grave.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Trotsky_grave.jpg)

Leon Trotsky's grave in [Coyoacán](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coyoac%C3%A1n "Coyoacán"), where his ashes are buried

In 1923, the historic town of [Gatchina](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gatchina "Gatchina") in [Petrograd Governorate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Petrograd_Governorate "Petrograd Governorate") (now [Leningrad Oblast](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leningrad_Oblast "Leningrad Oblast")) was renamed Trotsk ([Russian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_language "Russian language"): Троцк) by the Soviet authorities after Lev Trotsky.<sup id="cite_ref-GatchinskyUyezdHist_367-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-GatchinskyUyezdHist-367">[356]</a></sup> After Joseph Stalin became General Secretary of the [Russian Communist Party (b)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union "Communist Party of the Soviet Union"), Trotsky was gradually exiled, and the town was renamed **Krasnogvardeysk** (Красногварде́йск, _Red Guard City_) in 1929. In 1944, to increase the morale of Russian troops, the town's historic name was restored.<sup id="cite_ref-DistrictHist_368-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-DistrictHist-368">[357]</a></sup>

Trotsky's house in Coyoacán has been preserved in much the same condition as it was on the day he was assassinated there, and is now the [Leon Trotsky House Museum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky_House_Museum "Leon Trotsky House Museum") in Mexico City, run by a board which included his grandson Esteban Volkov (1926–2023).<sup id="cite_ref-369"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-369">[358]</a></sup> Trotsky's grave is located on its grounds. The foundation "International Friends of the Leon Trotsky Museum" has been organized to raise funds to improve the museum further.

Shortly before his assassination, Trotsky agreed to sell the bulk of the papers he still had to [Harvard University](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harvard_University "Harvard University"). After his assassination, his widow, Natalya Sedova collected his remaining papers and shipped them to Harvard, and in the years following, Harvard managed to collect additional papers that had been hidden from both Soviet and Nazi agents in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-370"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-370">[359]</a></sup> These papers now occupy 65 feet (20 m) of shelf space in Harvard's [Houghton Library](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Houghton_Library "Houghton Library").<sup id="cite_ref-371"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-371">[360]</a></sup>

Trotsky was never [rehabilitated](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rehabilitation_(Soviet) "Rehabilitation (Soviet)") during the rule of the Soviet government, despite the [de-Stalinization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/De-Stalinization "De-Stalinization")\-era rehabilitation of most other [Old Bolsheviks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_Bolshevik "Old Bolshevik") killed during the Great Purges. His son, Sergei Sedov, who died in 1937, was rehabilitated in 1988, as was Nikolai Bukharin. Beginning in 1989, Trotsky's books, forbidden until 1987, were published in the Soviet Union.

Trotsky was rehabilitated on 16 June 2001 by the [General Prosecutor's Office](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prosecutor_General_of_Russia "Prosecutor General of Russia") of the Russian Federation (Certificates of Rehabilitation No. 13/2182-90, No. 13-2200-99 in Archives Research Center "Memorial").<sup id="cite_ref-372"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-372">[361]</a></sup>

Trinidadian historian [CLR James](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CLR_James "CLR James") wrote, in the aftermath of Trotsky's death, that he evoked strong feelings of enmity and fear from several political figures. According to James, this included [Joseph Stalin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_Stalin "Joseph Stalin"), [Adolf Hitler](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adolf_Hitler "Adolf Hitler") and [Winston Churchill](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Winston_Churchill "Winston Churchill") because "these men knew his stature, the power of what he stood for, and were never lulled by the smallness of his forces".<sup id="cite_ref-373"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-373">[362]</a></sup>

Historian [Harold Shukman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harold_Shukman "Harold Shukman") assessed the conflicting perspectives on Trotsky's legacy in the Soviet Union and the [Western world](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_world "Western world"). He also commented on the lack of a balanced view. Specifically, he stated:

> Trotsky's legacy, unlike those of Stalin and Lenin, had long been submerged and obliterated as a topic of debate, and his place in Soviet history books had correspondingly diminished to one of no importance. For Western readers, however, Trotsky has always been one of the most enigmatic and powerful personalities of the Russian revolution, a Mephistophelian figure whose life ended in an appropriately dramatic way.<sup id="cite_ref-374"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-374">[363]</a></sup>

Political theorist David North attributed his diminished influence and historical role to the "virtually unlimited resources of the Soviet regime, and of [Stalinist-run](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marxism-Leninism "Marxism-Leninism") parties throughout the world, \[which\] were devoted to blackguarding Trotsky as an anti-Soviet saboteur, terrorist and fascist agent. Within the Soviet Union, his political co-thinkers, past and present, were ruthlessly exterminated".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENorth2010160–161_375-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTENorth2010160%E2%80%93161-375">[364]</a></sup> North was also critical of the biographical literature on Trotsky's legacy written by some historians such as [Ian Thatcher](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ian_Thatcher "Ian Thatcher"), Geoffrey Swain and Robert Service. He viewed these recent trends in historiography as "manifestations of the confluence of [neo-Stalinist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neo-Stalinist "Neo-Stalinist") falsification and traditional Anglo-American [anti-Communism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-Communism "Anti-Communism")".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENorth2010127_376-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTENorth2010127-376">[365]</a></sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Ludwig_Binder_Haus_der_Geschichte_Studentenrevolte_1968_2001_03_0275.4212_%2817086177105%29.jpg/220px-Ludwig_Binder_Haus_der_Geschichte_Studentenrevolte_1968_2001_03_0275.4212_%2817086177105%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Ludwig_Binder_Haus_der_Geschichte_Studentenrevolte_1968_2001_03_0275.4212_(17086177105).jpg)

[West German students](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_German_student_movement "West German student movement") holding a placard of Trotsky in 1968

In 2018, John Kelly wrote that "almost 80 years after Leon Trotsky founded the Fourth International, there are now Trotskyite organisations in 57 countries, including most of [Western Europe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_Europe "Western Europe") and [Latin America](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latin_America "Latin America")". However, he also argued that no Trotskyite group had ever led a revolution or built an enduring mass political party.<sup id="cite_ref-377"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-377">[366]</a></sup>

Robert Alexander made a similar observation in 1991 that Trotskyists had never assumed power in any nation but explained that the international movement did "not enjoy the support of a well-established regime, as did the heirs of Stalinism". Alexander also recognised that the "persistence of the movement in a [wide variety of countries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trotskyism#Trotskyist_movements "Trotskyism")" and the instability of political events across most of the world means the "possibility that a Trotskyist party might come to power in the foreseeable future cannot be totally ruled out".<sup id="cite_ref-378"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-378">[367]</a></sup>

On the other hand, British historian and socialist Christian Høgsbjerg believed that academic literature on Trotskyism had minimised its historical role in building wider social movements. Høgsbjerg stressed the key role of British Trotskyists in various movements such as the [Vietnam Solidarity Campaign](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vietnam_Solidarity_Campaign "Vietnam Solidarity Campaign") (1966–71), the [Anti-Nazi League](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-Nazi_League "Anti-Nazi League") (1977–81), the [Anti Poll Tax Federation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/All_Britain_Anti-Poll_Tax_Federation "All Britain Anti-Poll Tax Federation") (1989–91) and the [Stop the War Coalition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stop_the_War_Coalition "Stop the War Coalition") (2001).<sup id="cite_ref-379"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-379">[368]</a></sup>

Outside of the Fourth International, Trotsky has also been admired by a range of figures across intellectual, military, political and cultural fields including philosopher [Jean-Paul Satre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jean-Paul_Satre "Jean-Paul Satre"),<sup id="cite_ref-380"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-380">[369]</a></sup> military general [Mikhail Tukhachevsky](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mikhail_Tukhachevsky "Mikhail Tukhachevsky"),<sup id="cite_ref-381"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-381">[370]</a></sup> Marxist theorist [Rosa Luxemburg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rosa_Luxemburg "Rosa Luxemburg"),<sup id="cite_ref-382"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-382">[371]</a></sup> economist [Paul Sweezy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Sweezy "Paul Sweezy"),<sup id="cite_ref-383"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-383">[372]</a></sup> philosopher [John Dewey](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Dewey "John Dewey"),<sup id="cite_ref-384"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-384">[373]</a></sup> historian [A.J.P Taylor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/A.J.P_Taylor "A.J.P Taylor"),<sup id="cite_ref-385"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-385">[374]</a></sup> psychoanalyst [Erich Fromm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Erich_Fromm "Erich Fromm"),<sup id="cite_ref-386"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-386">[375]</a></sup> philosopher [Alasdair MacIntyre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alasdair_MacIntyre "Alasdair MacIntyre"),<sup id="cite_ref-387"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-387">[376]</a></sup> literary critic [Edmund Wilson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edmund_Wilson "Edmund Wilson"),<sup id="cite_ref-388"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-388">[377]</a></sup> painter [Diego Rivera](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diego_Rivera "Diego Rivera"),<sup id="cite_ref-389"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-389">[378]</a></sup> political leader [Martin Tranmæl](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Martin_Tranm%C3%A6l "Martin Tranmæl")<sup id="cite_ref-390"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-390">[379]</a></sup> and literary writer [Lu Xun](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lu_Xun "Lu Xun").<sup id="cite_ref-391"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-391">[380]</a></sup>

## Historical reputation\[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Leon_Trotsky&action=edit&section=44 "Edit section: Historical reputation")\]

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/8f/Trotskyportrait.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Trotskyportrait.jpg)

Posthumous portrait of Trotsky

In modern historiography, Trotsky's legacy has evoked a range of conflicting and diverse views.<sup id="cite_ref-books.google.com_392-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-books.google.com-392">[381]</a></sup> Biographer Paul Le Blanc stated "for millions of people throughout the world, Trotsky was initially seen as a [revolutionary](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Revolutionary "Revolutionary") [liberator](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emancipation "Emancipation")".<sup id="cite_ref-books.google.com_392-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-books.google.com-392">[381]</a></sup> He was viewed by contemporaries in the initial Soviet period and later historians as the [hero](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hero "Hero") of the [revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Revolution "Revolution").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1996272Rubenstein2011a96Thatcher2003100–105Carr19781–167Deutscher2015a310,_629_393-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1996272Rubenstein2011a96Thatcher2003100%E2%80%93105Carr19781%E2%80%93167Deutscher2015a310,_629-393">[382]</a></sup> Historian Betrand Patenaunde also noted his social appeal among the [Petrograd](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Petrograd "Petrograd") workers in which he drew "vast crowds of [workers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Working_class "Working class"), [soldiers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soldiers "Soldiers") and [sailors](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sailors "Sailors") in Petrograd with his spellbinding [oratory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rhetoric "Rhetoric") in 1917".<sup id="cite_ref-394"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-394">[383]</a></sup>

In the Soviet Union, his reputation gradually deteriorated over the course of the succession struggle as his views were presented as sectarian and [anti-Leninist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-Leninist "Anti-Leninist").<sup id="cite_ref-Trotsky_395-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-Trotsky-395">[384]</a></sup> Throughout the Stalin era, his name and image would be erased from history [books](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Books "Books"), [museums](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Museums "Museums") and [films](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Films "Films"). At the same time, Trotsky became a convenient bogeyman for Soviet affairs and was associated with ideological [heresy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heresy "Heresy").<sup id="cite_ref-396"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-396">[385]</a></sup> The works of Trotsky also remained banned until the Gorbachev era.<sup id="cite_ref-397"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-397">[386]</a></sup> Following the [de-Stalinization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/De-Stalinization "De-Stalinization") period, later generations of Soviet and Russian historians would reevaluate his role in the history of the revolution with varying interpretations.<sup id="cite_ref-Trotsky_395-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-Trotsky-395">[384]</a></sup>

Scholarly consensus holds Trotsky to have demonstrated remarkable leadership of the Red Army during the Civil War.<sup id="cite_ref-398"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-398">[387]</a></sup> He had been awarded the [Order of the Red Banner](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Order_of_the_Red_Banner "Order of the Red Banner") for his role in the Red Army such as [organising the defence of Petrograd](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Petrograd "Battle of Petrograd") when other members of the Bolshevik leadership were prepared to abandon the former capital.<sup id="cite_ref-399"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-399">[388]</a></sup> According to military scholar, [William C. Martel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_C._Martel "William C. Martel"), scholars view Trotsky as "one of the outstanding figures in modern [military history](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Military_history "Military history")" and a "directing [genius](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genius "Genius")".<sup id="cite_ref-400"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-400">[389]</a></sup> Swain asserted that the Bolsheviks would certainly have lost the Civil War within a single year without Trotsky as leader of the Red Army.<sup id="cite_ref-401"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-401">[390]</a></sup>

A number of scholars and Western socialists have argued that Trotsky represented a more [democratic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Democracy "Democracy"), [alternative](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-Stalinist_Left "Anti-Stalinist Left") to Stalin with particular emphasis drawn to his activities in the pre-Civil War period and as leader of the Left Opposition.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDaniels2008b189–198Barnett2013b101Rogovin2021b1–15Day1990159–188Deutscher2015a674–676,_1558_402-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDaniels2008b189%E2%80%93198Barnett2013b101Rogovin2021b1%E2%80%9315Day1990159%E2%80%93188Deutscher2015a674%E2%80%93676,_1558-402">[391]</a></sup> Prior to the October Revolution, Trotsky had been part of an old [radical democracy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radical_democracy "Radical democracy") which included both Left Mensheviks and Left Bolsheviks.<sup id="cite_ref-403"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-403">[392]</a></sup> He had also proposed the election of a new Soviet [presidium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Presidium "Presidium") with other [socialist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Socialist "Socialist") parties on the basis of [proportional representation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proportional_representation "Proportional representation") in September 1917.<sup id="cite_ref-404"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-404">[393]</a></sup> Deutscher described Trotsky as the "[Soviet's moving spirit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saint_Petersburg_Soviet "Saint Petersburg Soviet")" in 1905 and highlighted his representation of Bolsheviks, Mensheviks and the rest of the Soviets on major occasions.<sup id="cite_ref-Verso_Books_405-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-Verso_Books-405">[394]</a></sup> Rogovin stated that the Left Opposition, led by Trotsky, was a political movement that "offered a real alternative to Stalinism, and that to crush this movement was the primary function of the [Stalinist terror](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Terror "Great Terror")". He also attributed the eventual formation of a [one-party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/One-party "One-party") system to the [conditions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_civil_war "Russian civil war") which were "imposed on Bolshevism by hostile political forces".<sup id="cite_ref-406"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-406">[395]</a></sup>

Conversely, other figures such as Volkogonov have strongly criticised his defence of the Red Terror and dictatorship of the proletariat.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1996xxiii_407-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1996xxiii-407">[396]</a></sup> Service argued that his "ideas and practices laid several foundation stones for the erection of the Stalinist political, economic, social and even cultural edifice".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEService20093_408-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService20093-408">[397]</a></sup> Cherniaev considered Trotsky to be partly responsible for the establishment of a one-party, [authoritarian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian "Authoritarian") state and initiating several military practices such as summary executions which later became standard practice during the Stalinist era.<sup id="cite_ref-auto2_147-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-auto2-147">[144]</a></sup> Thatcher cited his defence of terror in his work, _[Terrorism and Communism: A Reply to Karl Kautsky](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Terrorism_and_Communism:_A_Reply_to_Karl_Kautsky "Terrorism and Communism: A Reply to Karl Kautsky"),_ but also acknowledged that Trotsky was capable of [leniency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pardon "Pardon") and had personally urged that White army deserters be treated with understanding.<sup id="cite_ref-409"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-409">[398]</a></sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Trotsky_Bust_%28by_Duncan_Ferguson%29_with_Photos_-_Leon_Trotsky_Museum_-_Coyoacan_-_Mexico_City_-_Mexico_%2815517085251%29.jpg/250px-Trotsky_Bust_%28by_Duncan_Ferguson%29_with_Photos_-_Leon_Trotsky_Museum_-_Coyoacan_-_Mexico_City_-_Mexico_%2815517085251%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Trotsky_Bust_(by_Duncan_Ferguson)_with_Photos_-_Leon_Trotsky_Museum_-_Coyoacan_-_Mexico_City_-_Mexico_(15517085251).jpg)

Bust of Trotsky at the [Leon Trotsky House Museum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky_House_Museum "Leon Trotsky House Museum") in [Mexico City](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mexico_City "Mexico City"), [Mexico](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mexico "Mexico")

This view has been disputed by some writers such as French socialist historian [Pierre Broue](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pierre_Broue "Pierre Broue") who criticised Western representations of Trotsky's role in the [Kronstadt rebellion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kronstadt_rebellion "Kronstadt rebellion") which he argued had falsely presented Trotsky as the principal figure that led and was responsible for the repression. He also added that [military tribunals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Military_tribunals "Military tribunals") and executions for desertions were a common feature of every war and not exclusive to the actions of the Red Army under Trotsky.<sup id="cite_ref-410"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-410">[399]</a></sup> Dukes believed Trotsky had been maligned and [caricatured](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caricatured "Caricatured") as a historical figure which necessitated a historical reappraisal.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Trotsky_reappraisal_317-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-The_Trotsky_reappraisal-317">[306]</a></sup> Patenaude regarded Service's characterisation of Trotsky as a "mass murderer and a terrorist" to be reflective of a wider attempt to [discredit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Character_assassination "Character assassination") Trotsky as a historical figure and noted his work featured several inaccuracies and distortions of the historical record.<sup id="cite_ref-411"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-411">[400]</a></sup> Daniels argued that many of the distinctive features of Stalin's rule such as his campaigns against "[bourgeois experts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Technician "Technician")" as seen with "the [Shakhty trials](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shakhty_Trial "Shakhty Trial"), his contemptuous [anti-intellectualism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-intellectualism "Anti-intellectualism") and the [dogmatization of Marxism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dogma "Dogma"), [the purges](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Purges_of_the_Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union "Purges of the Communist Party of the Soviet Union")—run totally counter to Trotsky's thought".<sup id="cite_ref-412"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-412">[401]</a></sup>

Various historians have credited Trotsky and the Left Opposition with shifting the Soviet economic orientation from the [NEP](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Economic_Policy "New Economic Policy") policy towards a [planned economy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Planned_economy "Planned economy") through their proposals for mass industrialization.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECarrDavies1971199Phillips200023Fitzpatrick2008110PaynePhillips20131936McDermott200661Lee20058Deutscher2003b468_413-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTECarrDavies1971199Phillips200023Fitzpatrick2008110PaynePhillips20131936McDermott200661Lee20058Deutscher2003b468-413">[402]</a></sup> Trotsky had delivered a joint report to the April Plenum of the Central Committee in 1926 which proposed a program for national industrialization and the replacement of annual plans with [five-year plans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Five-year_plans_of_the_Soviet_Union "Five-year plans of the Soviet Union"). His proposals were rejected by the Central Committee majority which was controlled by the troika and derided by Stalin at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-414"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-414">[403]</a></sup> The eventual adoption of the five year plans in 1928 would serve as the basis for Soviet [modernization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economic_development "Economic development").<sup id="cite_ref-415"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-415">[404]</a></sup> On the whole, historian Mark Sandle characterised his vision for socialist construction as “more [industrialist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Industrialisation "Industrialisation"), [modernist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Modernity "Modernity"), centralising and technocratic” than the economic proposals presented by rival theoretician Bukharin.<sup id="cite_ref-416"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-416">[405]</a></sup>

Several scholars have regarded his historical writings on the Soviet bureaucracy as having a considerable influence in shaping the receptive, attitudes of later Marxists and many non-Marxists. Trotsky associated bureaucratism with authoritarianism, excessive [centralism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Centralism "Centralism") and [conservatism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conservatism "Conservatism"). Political scientist Baruch Knei-Paz argued that Trotsky had done more than any other political figure to "show the historical and social roots of Stalinism" as a bureaucratic system.<sup id="cite_ref-417"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-417">[406]</a></sup> British [cybernetician](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cybernetician "Cybernetician") [Stafford Beer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stafford_Beer "Stafford Beer") who worked on a decentralized form of economic planning, [Project Cybersyn](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Project_Cybersyn "Project Cybersyn") from 1970 to 1973, was reported to have read and been influenced by Trotsky's critique of the [Soviet bureaucracy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nomenklatura "Nomenklatura").<sup id="cite_ref-418"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-418">[407]</a></sup> Other historians have noted the literary value of his account of historical events and social analysis with works such as _1905_ and _[The History of the Russian Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_History_of_the_Russian_Revolution "The History of the Russian Revolution")_ for wider historiography.<sup id="cite_ref-419"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-419">[408]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-420"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-420">[409]</a></sup>

## Political ideology and contributions to Marxist theory\[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Leon_Trotsky&action=edit&section=45 "Edit section: Political ideology and contributions to Marxist theory")\]

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b0/Trotsky_reading_The_Militant%2C_circa_1936.jpg/220px-Trotsky_reading_The_Militant%2C_circa_1936.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Trotsky_reading_The_Militant,_circa_1936.jpg)

Trotsky reading [The Militant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Militant "The Militant"), a socialist newsweekly, circa 1936

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Lev_Trotsky_1906-3.3_V1.jpg/250px-Lev_Trotsky_1906-3.3_V1.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Lev_Trotsky_1906-3.3_V1.jpg)

The [Soviet of Workers' Deputies of St. Petersburg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saint_Petersburg_Soviet "Saint Petersburg Soviet") in 1905, Trotsky in the center. The [soviets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_(council) "Soviet (council)") were an early example of a [workers council](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Workers_council "Workers council").

Trotsky considered himself to be a "Bolshevik-Leninist",<sup id="cite_ref-421"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-421">[410]</a></sup> arguing for the establishment of a [vanguard party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vanguard_party "Vanguard party"). He viewed himself as an advocate of [orthodox Marxism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orthodox_Marxism "Orthodox Marxism").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECox199284_422-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTECox199284-422">[411]</a></sup> Trotsky also adhered to [scientific socialism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scientific_socialism "Scientific socialism") and viewed this as a conscious expression of historical processes.<sup id="cite_ref-423"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-423">[412]</a></sup>

His politics differed in some aspects from those of Stalin or [Mao Zedong](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mao_Zedong "Mao Zedong"), most importantly in his rejection of the theory of "socialism in one country" and his declaring of the need for an international "permanent revolution". Numerous Fourth Internationalist groups around the world continue to describe themselves as Trotskyists and see themselves as standing in this tradition. However, they have different interpretations of the conclusions to be drawn from this.

Supporters of the Fourth International echo Trotsky's opposition to Stalinist [totalitarianism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Totalitarianism "Totalitarianism"), advocating political revolution and arguing that socialism cannot sustain itself without democracy.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERee1998_424-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTERee1998-424">[413]</a></sup> In particular, Trotsky called for the restoration of the right of criticism in areas such as [economic matters](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economic_policy "Economic policy"), the revitalization of [trade unions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trade_unions "Trade unions") and free elections of the [Soviet parties](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_political_parties_in_the_Soviet_Union "List of political parties in the Soviet Union").<sup id="cite_ref-425"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-425">[414]</a></sup>

Trotsky also formulated a theory of fascism based on a dialectical interpretation of events to analyze the manifestation of [Italian fascism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italian_fascism "Italian fascism") and the early emergence of Nazi Germany from 1930 to 1933.<sup id="cite_ref-426"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-426">[415]</a></sup>

### Economic programme\[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Leon_Trotsky&action=edit&section=46 "Edit section: Economic programme")\]

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fd/Graph_illustrating_the_Scissors_Crisis.png/300px-Graph_illustrating_the_Scissors_Crisis.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Graph_illustrating_the_Scissors_Crisis.png)

The Scissor crisis: retail and wholesale prices of agricultural and industrial goods in the Soviet Union July 1922 to November 1923

Trotsky was an early proponent of economic planning since 1923 and favored an accelerated pace of industrialization.<sup id="cite_ref-Twiss_427-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-Twiss-427">[416]</a></sup> In 1921, he had also been a prominent supporter of [Gosplan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gosplan "Gosplan") as a newly established body and called for the strengthening of its formal responsibilities to support a balanced level of economic reconstruction after the Civil War.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2015a587_428-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2015a587-428">[417]</a></sup> Trotsky also urged economic [decentralisation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decentralisation "Decentralisation") between the state, [oblast](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oblast "Oblast") regions and factories to counter structural inefficiency and the problem of bureaucracy.<sup id="cite_ref-429"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-429">[418]</a></sup>

Originally, he had proposed the principles underlying the [N.E.P.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Economic_Policy "New Economic Policy") in 1921 to the [Politbureau](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Politbureau "Politbureau") to mitigate urgent economic matters arising from war communism. He would later reproach Lenin privately about the delayed government response in 1922-1923.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2015a414–415_430-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2015a414%E2%80%93415-430">[419]</a></sup> However, his position differed from the majority of Soviet leaders at the time who fully supported the [New Economic policy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Economic_policy "New Economic policy").<sup id="cite_ref-Twiss_427-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-Twiss-427">[416]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-431"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-431">[420]</a></sup>

Comparatively, Trotsky believed that planning and N.E.P should develop within a mixed framework until the socialist sector gradually superseded the private industry.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2015a646_432-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2015a646-432">[421]</a></sup> He found allies among a circle of economic theorists and administrators which included [Evgenii Preobazhensky](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yevgeni_Preobrazhensky "Yevgeni Preobrazhensky") and [Georgy Pyatakov](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Georgy_Pyatakov "Georgy Pyatakov"), deputy chairman of the [Council of the National Economy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supreme_Soviet_of_the_National_Economy "Supreme Soviet of the National Economy").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2015a592_433-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2015a592-433">[422]</a></sup> More broadly, [intellectuals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intellectuals "Intellectuals") would constitute the core of the Left Opposition during the succession period.<sup id="cite_ref-434"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-434">[423]</a></sup>

Trotsky had specified the need for the "overall guidance in planning i.e. the systematic co-ordination of the fundamental sectors of the state economy in the process of adapting to the present market" and urged for a national plan<sup id="cite_ref-435"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-435">[424]</a></sup> alongside currency stabilization.<sup id="cite_ref-436"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-436">[425]</a></sup> He also rejected the Stalinist conception of industrialisation which favoured [heavy industry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heavy_industry "Heavy industry"). Rather, he proposed the use of [foreign trade](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Foreign_trade "Foreign trade") as an accelerator and to direct investments by means of a system of comparative [coefficients](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coefficients "Coefficients").<sup id="cite_ref-437"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-437">[426]</a></sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/%D0%9B._%D0%94._%D0%A2%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%86%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9%2C_%D0%9B._%D0%91._%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B5%D0%B2_%D0%B8_%D0%93._%D0%95._%D0%97%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%8C%D0%B5%D0%B2._%D0%A1%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%B4%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B0_1920-%D1%85_%D0%B3%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%BE%D0%B2.jpg/250px-%D0%9B._%D0%94._%D0%A2%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%86%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9%2C_%D0%9B._%D0%91._%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B5%D0%B2_%D0%B8_%D0%93._%D0%95._%D0%97%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%8C%D0%B5%D0%B2._%D0%A1%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%B4%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B0_1920-%D1%85_%D0%B3%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%BE%D0%B2.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:%D0%9B._%D0%94._%D0%A2%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%86%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9,_%D0%9B._%D0%91._%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B5%D0%B2_%D0%B8_%D0%93._%D0%95._%D0%97%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%8C%D0%B5%D0%B2._%D0%A1%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%B4%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B0_1920-%D1%85_%D0%B3%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%BE%D0%B2.jpg)

Trotsky, [Kamenev](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kamenev "Kamenev") and [Zinoviev](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zinoviev "Zinoviev") pictured in the mid-1920s as members of the United Opposition

Trotsky and the Left Opposition developed a number of economic proposals in response to the [scissor crisis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scissor_crisis "Scissor crisis") which had undermined relations between the workers and peasants in 1923–1924. This included a [progressive tax](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Progressive_tax "Progressive tax") on the wealthier sections of populations such as the [kulaks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kulak "Kulak") and [NEPmen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NEPmen "NEPmen") alongside an equilibrium of the import-export balance to access accumulated reserves to purchase machinery from abroad to increase the pace of industrialization.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMandel199562_438-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMandel199562-438">[427]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-439"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-439">[428]</a></sup>

The policy was later adopted by members of the United Opposition which also advocated a programme of rapid industrialization during the debates of 1924 and 1927. The United Opposition proposed a progressive tax on wealthier peasants, the encouragement of [agricultural cooperatives](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agricultural_cooperatives "Agricultural cooperatives") and the formation of collective farms on a voluntary basis.<sup id="cite_ref-440"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-440">[429]</a></sup>

Trotsky as president of the [electrification](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electrification "Electrification") commission along with members of the Opposition bloc had put forward an electrification plan which involved the construction of the [hydroelectric](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hydroelectric "Hydroelectric") [Dnieprostroi dam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dnieper_Hydroelectric_Station "Dnieper Hydroelectric Station").<sup id="cite_ref-441"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-441">[430]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-442"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-442">[431]</a></sup> He had also warned against the danger of market spontaneity and called for a well-thought out strategy of [commercial balance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commercial_balance "Commercial balance"). Overall, Trotsky was sharply critical of Bukharin and Stalin's views on the state of the Soviet economy. Russian historian, Vladimir Buldakov found that some historical research had supported the view that Trotsky advocated the most rational decisions for industrial development.<sup id="cite_ref-443"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-443">[432]</a></sup>

In 1932–33, Trotsky maintained the need for mass participation in the operationalisation of the planned economy.<sup id="cite_ref-444"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-444">[433]</a></sup> He elaborated on the need of [Soviet democracy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_democracy "Soviet democracy") for the [industrialization period](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Industrialization_in_the_Soviet_Union "Industrialization in the Soviet Union") when questioned by the Dewey Commission in 1937:

> The successes are very important, and I affirmed it every time. They are due to the abolition of private property and to the possibilities inherent in [planned economy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Planned_economy "Planned economy"). But, they – I cannot say exactly – but I will say two or three times less than they could be under a regime of Soviet democracy<sup id="cite_ref-445"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-445">[434]</a></sup>

According to Fitzpatrick, the scholarly consensus was that Stalin appropriated the position of the Left Opposition on such matters as [industrialisation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Industrialisation "Industrialisation") and [collectivisation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Collectivisation "Collectivisation").<sup id="cite_ref-446"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-446">[435]</a></sup> Other scholars have argued that the economic programme of Trotsky differed from the forced [policy of collectivisation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Collectivization_in_the_Soviet_Union "Collectivization in the Soviet Union") implemented by Stalin after 1928 due to the levels of brutality associated with its enforcement.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMandel199559_447-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMandel199559-447">[436]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Yale_University_Press_320-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-Yale_University_Press-320">[309]</a></sup>

### Permanent Revolution\[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Leon_Trotsky&action=edit&section=47 "Edit section: Permanent Revolution")\]

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Diego_rivera_Commies.jpg/250px-Diego_rivera_Commies.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Diego_rivera_Commies.jpg)

A [Diego Rivera](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diego_Rivera "Diego Rivera") mural (_[Man, Controller of the Universe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Man,_Controller_of_the_Universe "Man, Controller of the Universe")_) depicts Trotsky with [Marx](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marx "Marx") and [Engels](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Engels "Engels") as a true champion of the workers' struggle

The Permanent Revolution concept is the theory that the [bourgeois](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bourgeois "Bourgeois") democratic tasks in countries with delayed bourgeois democratic development can only be accomplished through the establishment of a workers' state, and that the creation of a workers' state would inevitably involve inroads against capitalist property. Thus, the accomplishment of bourgeois democratic tasks passes over into [proletarian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proletarian "Proletarian") tasks. Although most closely associated with Leon Trotsky, the call for a "Permanent Revolution" is first found in the writings of [Karl Marx](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx "Karl Marx") and [Friedrich Engels](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Friedrich_Engels "Friedrich Engels") in March 1850, in the aftermath of the [1848 Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1848_Revolution "1848 Revolution"), in their [Address](https://www.marxists.org/archive/marx/works/1847/communist-league/1850-ad1.htm) of the Central Committee to the [Communist League](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communist_League "Communist League"):

> It is our interest and our task to make the revolution permanent until all the more or less propertied classes have been driven from their ruling positions, until the proletariat has conquered state power and until the association of the proletarians has progressed sufficiently far—not only in one country but in all the leading countries of the world—that competition between the proletarians of these countries ceases and at least the decisive forces of production are concentrated in the hands of the workers. ... Their battle-cry must be: **The Permanent Revolution**.

Trotsky's conception of the Permanent Revolution is based on his understanding, drawing on the work of the founder of Russian Marxism [Georgy Plekhanov](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Georgy_Plekhanov "Georgy Plekhanov"), that in "backward" countries the tasks of the Bourgeois Democratic Revolution could not be achieved by the bourgeoisie itself. Trotsky first developed this conception in collaboration with Alexander Parvus in late 1904–1905. The relevant articles were later collected in Trotsky's books _1905_ and in "Permanent Revolution", which also contains his essay "[Results and Prospects](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Results_and_Prospects "Results and Prospects")." Some Trotskyists have argued that the state of the [Third World](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Third_World "Third World") shows that capitalism offers no way forward for underdeveloped countries, thus again proving the central tenet of the theory.<sup id="cite_ref-448"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-448">[437]</a></sup>

According to his biographer, Isaac Deutscher, Trotsky explicitly supported revolution through [proletarian internationalism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proletarian_internationalism "Proletarian internationalism") but was opposed to achieving this via [military](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Military "Military") [conquest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conquest "Conquest") with documented references made to his personal opposition to the [war with Poland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Soviet_War "Polish–Soviet War") in 1920, proposed armistice with the [Entente](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_I "Allies of World War I") and temperance with staging [anti-British revolts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_foreign_policy_in_the_Middle_East "British foreign policy in the Middle East") in the Middle East.<sup id="cite_ref-449"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-449">[438]</a></sup>

### United front\[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Leon_Trotsky&action=edit&section=48 "Edit section: United front")\]

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/1f/Fascism.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Fascism.png)

Leon Trotsky's original pamphlet _**"[Fascism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fascism "Fascism"): What it is and how to fight it"**_ published posthumously which elaborated on the need of a united front for mass mobilisation.

Trotsky was a central figure in the Comintern during its first four congresses. During this time, he helped to generalize the strategy and tactics of the Bolsheviks to newly formed Communist parties across Europe and further afield. From 1921 onwards, the [united front](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_front "United front"), a method of uniting revolutionaries and reformists in the common struggle while winning some of the workers to revolution, was the central tactic put forward by the Comintern after the defeat of the German revolution.

Trotsky was a strong critic of the shifting Comintern policy position under Stalin which directed German Communists to treat social democrats as "[social fascists](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_fascism "Social fascism")". Historian Bertrand Patenaude believed that the Comintern policy following the "[Great Break](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Break_(USSR) "Great Break (USSR)")" facilitated the rise of Hitler's party.<sup id="cite_ref-450"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-450">[439]</a></sup> Marxist theorist and economist [Hillel Ticktin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hillel_Ticktin "Hillel Ticktin") argued that Trotsky's political strategy and approach to fascism such as the emphasis on an organisational bloc between the [German Communist Party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Germany "Communist Party of Germany") and [Social-Democratic party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_Democratic_Party_of_Germany "Social Democratic Party of Germany") during the interwar period would very likely have prevented Hitler [from ascending to political power](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adolf_Hitler%27s_rise_to_power#Weimar_parties_fail_to_halt_Nazis "Adolf Hitler's rise to power").<sup id="cite_ref-451"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-451">[440]</a></sup>

After he was exiled and politically marginalized by Stalinism, Trotsky continued to argue for a united front against fascism in Germany and Spain. According to Joseph Choonara of the British [Socialist Workers Party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Socialist_Workers_Party_(UK) "Socialist Workers Party (UK)") in _[International Socialism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Socialism "International Socialism")_, his articles on the united front represent an essential part of his political legacy.<sup id="cite_ref-452"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-452">[441]</a></sup>

### Uneven and combined development\[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Leon_Trotsky&action=edit&section=49 "Edit section: Uneven and combined development")\]

The concept of uneven and combined development derived from the political theories of Trotsky.<sup id="cite_ref-453"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-453">[442]</a></sup> This concept was developed in combination with the related theory of permanent revolution to explain the historical context of Russia. He would later elaborate on this theory to explain the specific laws of uneven development in 1930 and the conditions for a possible revolutionary scenario.<sup id="cite_ref-454"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-454">[443]</a></sup> According to biographer Ian Thatcher, this theory would be later generalised to "the entire history of mankind".<sup id="cite_ref-455"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-455">[444]</a></sup>

Political scientists Emanuele Saccarelli and Latha Varadarajan valued his theory as a "signal contribution" to the discipline of [international relations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_relations "International relations"). They argued his theory presented "a specific understanding of capitalist development as 'uneven', insofar as it systematically featured geographically divergent 'advanced' and 'backward' regions" across the [world economy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_economy "World economy").<sup id="cite_ref-456"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-456">[445]</a></sup>

### Literary criticism and socialist culture\[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Leon_Trotsky&action=edit&section=50 "Edit section: Literary criticism and socialist culture")\]

> Faith merely promises to move mountains; but [technology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Technology "Technology"), which takes nothing ‘on faith’, is actually able to cut down mountains and move them. Up to now this was done for industrial purposes (mines) or for railways (tunnels); in the future this will be done on an immeasurably larger scale, according to a general industrial and [artistic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artistic "Artistic") plan. Man will occupy himself with re-registering mountains and rivers, and will earnestly and repeatedly make improvements in [nature](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nature "Nature").

—Trotsky, _Literature and Revolution_, 1924<sup id="cite_ref-457"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-457">[446]</a></sup>

In _[Literature and Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Literature_and_Revolution "Literature and Revolution")_, Trotsky examined aesthetic issues in relation to class and the Russian revolution. Soviet scholar Robert Bird considered his work as the "first systematic treatment of art by a Communist leader" and a catalyst for later, Marxist cultural and critical theories.<sup id="cite_ref-458"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-458">[447]</a></sup> He would later co-author the 1938 _[Manifesto for an Independent Revolutionary Art](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manifesto_for_an_Independent_Revolutionary_Art "Manifesto for an Independent Revolutionary Art")_ with the signed endorsement of [Andre Breton](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Andre_Breton "Andre Breton") and Rivera.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2015a1474_459-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeutscher2015a1474-459">[448]</a></sup> Trotsky's writings on literature such as his 1923 survey which advocated tolerance, limited censorship and respect for literary tradition had strong appeal to the [New York Intellectuals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_York_Intellectuals "New York Intellectuals").<sup id="cite_ref-460"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-460">[449]</a></sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Trotsky_Annenkow_1922_cartoon.jpg/196px-Trotsky_Annenkow_1922_cartoon.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Trotsky_Annenkow_1922_cartoon.jpg)

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Trotsky-Annenkov_1921_Red_Army.jpg/138px-Trotsky-Annenkov_1921_Red_Army.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Trotsky-Annenkov_1921_Red_Army.jpg)

Trotsky presented a critique of contemporary literary movements such as [Futurism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Futurism "Futurism") and emphasised a need of cultural autonomy for the development of a socialist culture.
