According to literary critic [Terry Eagleton](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Terry_Eagleton "Terry Eagleton"), Trotsky recognised "like Lenin on the need for a socialist culture to absorb the finest products of bourgeois art".<sup id="cite_ref-461"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-461">[450]</a></sup> Trotsky himself viewed the proletarian culture as "temporary and transitional" which would provide the foundations for a culture above classes. He also argued that the pre-conditions for artistic creativity were economic well-being and emancipation from material constraints.<sup id="cite_ref-Oxford_Eng._:_Clarendon_Press_462-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-Oxford_Eng._:_Clarendon_Press-462">[451]</a></sup>

Political scientist Baruch Knei-Paz characterised [his view](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Social_and_Political_Thought_of_Leon_Trotsky "The Social and Political Thought of Leon Trotsky") on the role of the party as transmitters of culture to the masses and raising the standards of education, as well as entry into the cultural sphere, but that the process of artistic creation in terms of language and presentation should be the domain of the practitioner. Knei-Paz also noted key distinctions between Trotsky's approach on cultural matters and [Stalin's policy in the 1930s](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Socialist_realism#Stalin_era "Socialist realism").<sup id="cite_ref-Oxford_Eng._:_Clarendon_Press_462-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-Oxford_Eng._:_Clarendon_Press-462">[451]</a></sup>

## In popular culture\[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Leon_Trotsky&action=edit&section=51 "Edit section: In popular culture")\]

-   The comedic film, _[The Trotsky](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Trotsky "The Trotsky")_, centers on a protagonist named Leon Bronstein, played by [Jay Baruchel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jay_Baruchel "Jay Baruchel"), who believes himself to be the reincarnation of Leon Trotsky.<sup id="cite_ref-463"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-463">[452]</a></sup>
-   The characters of [Snowball](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Snowball_(Animal_Farm) "Snowball (Animal Farm)") and [Emmanuel Goldstein](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emmanuel_Goldstein "Emmanuel Goldstein") in [George Orwell](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_Orwell "George Orwell")'s novels, _[Animal Farm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Animal_Farm "Animal Farm")_ and _[Nineteen Eighty-Four](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nineteen_Eighty-Four "Nineteen Eighty-Four")_ respectively, are based on Trotsky.<sup id="cite_ref-464"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-464">[453]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-465"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-465">[454]</a></sup>
-   Trotsky's final days and death was dramatized in the 1972 film _[The Assassination of Trotsky](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Assassination_of_Trotsky "The Assassination of Trotsky")_, directed by [Joseph Losey](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_Losey "Joseph Losey") and starring [Richard Burton](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_Burton "Richard Burton") as Trotsky.<sup id="cite_ref-466"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-466">[455]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-467"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-467">[456]</a></sup>
-   The 8-episode biographical drama [Trotsky](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trotsky_(TV_series) "Trotsky (TV series)") debuted on the Russian [Channel One](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Channel_One_Russia "Channel One Russia") in 2017, [Netflix](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Netflix "Netflix") purchased the distribution rights to the series in 2018 and made it available on its platform.<sup id="cite_ref-468"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-468">[457]</a></sup>
-   1980s UK band [The Redskins](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Redskins "The Redskins") debut single was entitled "Lev Bronstein", released on the CNT [record label](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Record_label "Record label") in 1982.

## Notes\[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Leon_Trotsky&action=edit&section=53 "Edit section: Notes")\]

1.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_ref-1 "Jump up")** Trotsky was People's Commissar for Military Affairs from 14 March 1918 and People's Commissar for Naval Affairs from April 1918 before the offices were merged on 12 November 1923.
2.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_ref-4 "Jump up")** Russian: Лев "Лейба" Давидович Бронштейн, <small><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Romanization_of_Russian" title="Romanization of Russian">romanized:</a></small> _Lev "Leyba" Davidovich Bronshteyn_, IPA: [\[lʲef – lʲɪjbə – dɐˈvʲidəvʲɪtɕ brɐnʂˈtʲejn\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA/Russian "Help:IPA/Russian").
3.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_ref-6 "Jump up")** ;<sup id="cite_ref-5"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-5">[3]</a></sup> Russian: Лев Давидович Троцкий, <small><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Romanization_of_Russian" title="Romanization of Russian">romanized:</a></small> _Lev Davidovich Trotskiy_, IPA: [\[ˈlʲef ˈtrotskʲɪj\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA/Russian "Help:IPA/Russian") [](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/a/a2/Ru-Leon_Trotsky.ogg/Ru-Leon_Trotsky.ogg.mp3 "Play audio")<sup><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Ru-Leon_Trotsky.ogg" title="File:Ru-Leon Trotsky.ogg">ⓘ</a></sup>; Ukrainian: Лев Давидович Троцький; also transliterated _Lyev_, _Trotski_, _Trockij_ and _Trotzky_.
4.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_ref-150 "Jump up")** Yakov Sverdlov was the Central Committee's senior secretary responsible for personnel affairs from 1917 and until his death in March 1919. He was replaced by [Elena Stasova](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elena_Stasova "Elena Stasova"), and in November 1919 by Nikolai Krestinsky. After Krestinsky's ouster in March 1921, Vyacheslav Molotov became the senior secretary, but he lacked Krestinsky's authority, since he was not a full Politburo member. Stalin took over the position as senior secretary, which was formalized at the XIth Party Congress in April 1922, with Molotov becoming second secretary.
5.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_ref-151 "Jump up")** It is not clear why Kamenev, a mild-mannered man with few leadership ambitions and who was the brother-in-law of Trotsky, sided with Zinoviev and Stalin against Trotsky in 1922. Trotsky later speculated that it may have been due to Kamenev's love of comfort, which Trotsky found "repelled me." He expressed [his feelings to Kamenev](https://www.marxists.org/archive/trotsky/1939/xx/kremlin.htm) in late 1920 or early 1921:
    
    > Our relations with Kamenev, which were very good in the first period after the insurrection, began to become more distant from that day.
    
6.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_ref-152 "Jump up")** The Central Committee's Secretariat became increasingly important during the Civil War and especially in its aftermath, as the Party switched from elected officials to appointed ones. The change was prompted by the need to allocate manpower quickly during the Civil War as well as by the transformation of the party from a small group of revolutionaries into the country's ruling party, with a corresponding increase in membership. New members included career seekers and former members of banned socialist parties, who were viewed with apprehension by Old Bolsheviks.<sup>[<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> To prevent a possible degeneration of the party, various membership requirements were instituted for party officials, and the ultimate power of appointment of local officials was reserved for the Secretariat of the Central Committee. This put enormous power in the general secretary's hands.
7.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_ref-161 "Jump up")** Lenin's [letter](https://www.marxists.org/archive/lenin/works/1922/dec/15.htm) to Stalin dictated on 15 December 1922: "I am sure Trotsky will uphold my views as well as I." Faced with a united opposition by Lenin and Trotsky, the Central Committee reversed its previous decision and adopted the Lenin-Trotsky proposal.
8.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_ref-163 "Jump up")** Trotsky explained in Chapter 12 of his unfinished book [_Stalin_](http://maximumred.blogspot.com/2005_08_01_maximumred_archive.html) that he refused to deliver the report because "it seemed to me equivalent to announcing my candidacy for the role of Lenin's successor at a time when Lenin was fighting a grave illness.
9.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_ref-166 "Jump up")** Radek wrote:<sup id="cite_ref-165"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-165">[157]</a></sup>
    
    > The need of the hour was for a man who would incarnate the call to struggle, a man who, subordinating himself completely to the requirements of the struggle, would become the ringing summons to arms, the will which exacts from all unconditional submission to a great, sacrificial necessity. Only a man with Trotsky's capacity for work, only a man so unsparing of himself as Trotsky, only a man who knew how to speak to the soldiers as Trotsky did—only such a man could have become the standard bearer of the armed toilers. He was all things rolled into one.
    
10.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_ref-172 "Jump up")** The term "Trotskyism" was first coined by the Russian liberal politician Pavel Milyukov, the first foreign minister in the Provisional Government who, in April 1917, was forced to demand that the British government release Trotsky.
11.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_ref-239 "Jump up")** The murder weapon was an ice axe (and not an [ice pick](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ice_pick "Ice pick")—an awl-like bartender's tool); this misnomer has been explained as being occasioned by the assassin's use of the French-language term _picolet_—meaning the winter-mountaineering tool which resembles the [pickaxes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pickaxe "Pickaxe") used in mining and other excavations, and by the multiple languages spoken by those involved in reporting the details; many history and reference books have confused the two tools.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEConquest1992418_238-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_note-FOOTNOTEConquest1992418-238">[228]</a></sup>

Retrieved 17 December 2021. Trotsky was a leader of a small group, the Mezhraionts, consisting of almost four thousand members.

4.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_ref-7 "Jump up")** "A prolific writer and a spellbinding orator, he was a central figure in the Russian Revolution of 1905 and the October Revolution of 1917, the organizer and leader of the Red Army in the Russian Civil War, the heir apparent to Soviet leader Vladimir Lenin, and the arch enemy and then vanquished foe of Joseph Stalin in the succession struggle after Lenin's death".Patenaude, Betrand (21 September 2017). _"Trotsky and Trotskyism" in The Cambridge History of Communism: Volume 1, World Revolution and Socialism in One Country 1917–1941_. Cambridge University Press. p. 189. [ISBN](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ISBN_(identifier) "ISBN (identifier)") [978-1-108-21041-6](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1-108-21041-6 "Special:BookSources/978-1-108-21041-6").

93.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky#cite_ref-96 "Jump up")** For a time it was speculated that this letter was in fact not an authentic one. However, Trotsky's himself verified its authenticity to Wheeler-Bennett. [Wheeler-Bennett, John W.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Wheeler-Bennett "John Wheeler-Bennett") (1938). _Brest-Litovsk: the Forgotten Peace, March 1918_ (1st ed.). London: [Macmillan and Co., Limited](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Macmillan_Publishers "Macmillan Publishers"). pp. 185–186. The authenticity of this letter, which has been in doubt for twenty years, was personally confirmed to the writer by Leon Trotsky in conversation in Mexico City, in September 1937.; the letter was auctioned in 1990. Pyle, Richard (23 March 1990). ["Revolutionary's Letter to Lenin Auctioned"](https://apnews.com/article/346eacc1c0640c0659dc0d8edfb866e1). _[Associated Press](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Associated_Press "Associated Press")_.
